Peng Dehuai and Huang Gonglue Surrender 72

Huang Gonglue's Family Sent to Hunan as Hostages

Changsha dispatch: Communist bandit leaders Peng Dehuai and Huang Gonglue are both natives of Xiangtan County, Hunan. Peng was a student at the Baoding Military Academy, and Huang was a student at the Whampoa Military Academy. Both were subordinates of the former Division Commander Liu Xing. In 1928, Peng was a regimental commander and Huang a battalion commander, stationed in Pingjiang County. Due to a dispute over military pay, they led their troops in a mutiny, joining the Red bandits. Recently, they have entrusted people three times to express their willingness to surrender to He Jian, requesting to preserve their existing strength and be reorganized into two divisions, with Peng and Huang remaining as division commanders. He Jian, considering the matter of great importance, specially dispatched Chief of Staff Liu Yinggu to Nanjing to request instructions from the central government. The central government then appointed Huang Hanxiang as the military inspector for the three provinces of Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi, to handle this matter jointly with He Jian. Huang Hanxiang has been in Hunan for two months and has personally gone to Pingxiang and Ji'an, holding several consultations with Peng and Huang's representatives. Regarding Peng and Huang's request to preserve their troops, he has agreed to handle it with discretion. However, He Jian's intention is that Peng and Huang must demonstrate their anti-communist efforts in practice, cooperate with the National Army, and first carry out the suppression of Zhu De and Mao Zedong to atone for their crimes. Huang Gonglue's family originally hid in Shanghai. Now, to show sincerity, his elderly mother, wife, and two sons have been sent by people from Shanghai to Changsha, handed over to He Jian as hostages. He Jian has ordered them to temporarily reside in Huang Hanxiang's home, treating them with preferential care. Meanwhile, Huang Hanxiang will go to Ji'an again yesterday (23rd) to urge Peng and Huang to quickly eliminate Zhu De and Mao Zedong and lead their troops to return. At the same time, a written exhortation to Peng and Huang's subordinates, printed in 10,000 copies, has been dispatched by aircraft to Peng and Huang's bases in Donggu and Ningdu, Jiangxi, to enlighten them. The wording is as follows: "You were originally revolutionary troops. Unfortunately, due to circumstances, you were temporarily confused and plunged into the vortex of the Communist bandits. Over the years, you have suffered much hardship and committed many evils, abandoning your glorious past history and forfeiting your great future. You yourselves, in the quiet of the night, should search your hearts and weep bitterly. Now, in this final period of communist suppression, you are finally able to awaken and learn, showing that your conscience has not been extinguished and your situation is pitiable. According to the various things presented by the representatives you have sent repeatedly, we know that your environment is extremely difficult, and your return is truly sincere. The central government, being broad-minded, will not blame the past and will grant you a fresh start. Therefore, we have also resolutely agreed to your earnest request. Since you have expressed your sincerity to return, you should not fear obstacles or avoid difficulties, and you should demonstrate your aspirations in practice. Now, fearing that you still have doubts, we especially declare three things to you: (1) You have repeatedly sent representatives to negotiate, and Huang Gonglue has sent his mother and wife to Changsha, which shows that you are deeply repentant and eager to surrender. Now, the armies of the three provinces have been deployed steadily, advancing by land and water, encircling in separate directions, preparing to eliminate the bandits in one fell swoop. You should also take the opportunity to act quickly, cooperate in eliminating Zhu De, Mao Zedong, and other bandit troops, and atone for your crimes, as proof of your thorough repentance. (2) After your surrender, your lives can be absolutely guaranteed completely, and your troops can still exist. Your requests can be considered fully realized. (3) Huang Gonglue's elderly mother and wife, who have been sent to Changsha, are now being properly protected and treated preferentially. Do not worry about them. Your family members also hope that you will return soon to reunite and share the happiness of family life. The past, in all its forms, is like yesterday's death; the future, in all its forms, is like today's birth. Lay down the butcher knife and become a Buddha on the spot. A great opportunity is fleeting. We hope you will not hesitate or waver, and quickly implement your surrender plan and return to the embrace of the Three Principles of the People." (24th)

The 19th Route Army Vigorously Suppresses Jiangxi Bandits 73

Ma Brigade Recaptures Chongyi, Li Mingrui's Band Flees to Longquan

Guangzhou dispatch: Since Jiang Guangnai, commander-in-chief of the 19th Route Army, entered Jiangxi, he has been besieging the bandit troops in Ningdu for days. According to front-line news, Ningdu is the main base of the Zhu-Peng Communist bandits. Now, because the government troops are urgently surrounding Ningdu, the bandit troops have been fleeing in disarray towards Ruijin and Guangchang. The 12th and 22nd pseudo-armies of the Ningdu bandit troops have fled to Huangpi and Xiaobu. The bandit atmosphere in Ningdu has indeed been slightly suppressed, but the peasant bandits near Ningdu City are still rampant. The grain in the villages has been looted by the bandits, and not a single grain remains. Even the bandits themselves only cook one meal per person per day. Over a hundred refugees imprisoned in the Golden Essence Cave were all slaughtered by the bandits. Many women over the age of sixteen were forcibly remarried. The people in the bandit areas were forced to engrave the words "Reddened" on their arms, so even if they do not die at the hands of the bandits, it will be difficult for them to survive. Furthermore, the bandit party in Yudu, since being defeated, has been scarred everywhere, which is shocking. According to Yudu County Magistrate Wang Jingming's report, he led the people's militia from Luojiadu in the western township and Mufeng in the southern township at dawn on the 4th of this month and recovered Yudu City. In this battle, one pseudo-chairman, Huang Fosheng, was killed, one pseudo-captain, Jiang Luo, was beheaded, over ten important leaders were captured, sixty bandits were captured, and three to four hundred civilians who had been kidnapped by the bandits were released. The remaining bandits have now fled and gathered in the Wan'gang and Sanmen Tan areas west of Yudu. Currently, people's militias are being organized in the urban area and the three townships in the east, west, and south to defend key points. The city walls have been torn down to the ground, and slightly larger buildings have been burned to the ground. The people in the entire city, apart from those who fled and were killed by the bandits, only children under the age of ten and old women over the age of fifty remain. The stoves are cold and the households are silent, desolate and unbearable to witness, and even people of iron and stone should shed tears, and so on. The above is about the bandit disaster in eastern Jiangxi. As for the southern Jiangxi area, after places such as Shangyou were recovered, the people's frightened souls had just settled down. Unexpectedly, Li Mingrui's band fled from the Hunan border into Chongyi. Fortunately, the 19th Route Army had pre-emptively sent troops to defend and quickly rushed to support, and Chongyi was recovered. Li's bandits have now fled again to Longquan, Hunan. It was found that when Li's bandits fled to Chongyi this time, the 19th Route Army immediately dispatched Brigade Commander Ma Kun to lead the Ding Regiment and the First Battalion of the Yin Regiment in the rain from Nankang at 6:00 AM on the 3rd. They arrived at Yangmeisi at 7:00 PM to camp. Because the laborers were exhausted and according to the locals, the journey from Yangmeisi to Chongyi was eighty li, mostly consisting of high mountains and steep ridges. Brigade Commander Ma, in order to maintain combat effectiveness, consulted with the regimental and battalion commanders and advanced to Changlongxu on the 4th to camp. At 3:00 PM that afternoon, they arrived at the market town. They received a telegram from headquarters ordering them to occupy the line of the north gate of Chongyi before the 5th and launch a fierce attack on the bandits. The various units then departed from Changlongxu at 6:00 AM on the 5th and advanced towards Chongyi. At about 11:00 AM, the officers and soldiers of the Ding Regiment discovered a bandit sentry five li outside Chongyi City. Seeing the government troops approaching, Li Mingrui used a small force to cover the south gate, while he led the bandits to flee from the north. The Ding Regiment took advantage of the situation to pursue and attack outside the south gate, killing dozens of bandits and seizing more than eighty rifles. They then recovered Chongyi County on the same day at noon. (March 21st)

Zhu Peide Completes Inspection in Xuzhou 74

Xuzhou dispatch: Zhu Peide arrived in Xuzhou on the 22nd. On the 23rd, he held a military parade and separate academic examinations in two subjects. On the morning of the 24th, Zhu, along with inspection committee member Fan Yuhuang and others, inspected the internal affairs of the various units of the Seventh Division, guided by Wang Jun, Zeng Wanzhong, and others. They first inspected the cadre training team, then the division headquarters' special service company, then the 37th and 38th regiments and the 41st and 42nd regiments in the Jiulishan barracks, as well as the artillery and engineering battalions. The inspection items were personnel, horses, cleanliness, hygiene, artillery, ammunition, clothing, equipment, materials, etc. In the afternoon, live-fire shooting exercises were reviewed at Machang Lake, east of the large parade ground in front of Jiulishan. Several soldiers from each company were selected, and officers above the rank of major were present, totaling about five or six hundred people. The target distance was about two hundred meters. At the same time, earthwork operations were also practiced, including infantry kneeling trenches, standing trenches, single-person trenches, and artillery mountain gun shelters, mortar shelters, and machine gun shelters. It was not completed until late at night. On the 25th, from morning to noon, a field exercise was held, which was a confrontation between mixed regiments, divided into east and west armies. The east army was the 42nd Regiment, attached with an artillery company and an engineer platoon, commanded by Regimental Commander Chen Shaohan. The west army was the 37th Regiment, also attached with an artillery company and an engineer platoon, commanded by Regimental Commander Yi Kaizhen. Zhu Peide served as the commander, Fan Yuhuang served as the chief judge of the east army, and Kong Fanqing served as the chief judge of the west army. The commander's flag was a triangular red flag with a white square heart inside. The chief judge's flag was a triangular flag, red on the top and white on the bottom. Personnel in the commander's department and visitors all wore red cloth armbands as identification. The exercise subjects were attack, offensive defense, offensive transfer, and decisive battle, a total of four items. During the exercises, firecrackers were used instead of gunshots. On this day, before 10:00 AM, the east army stopped in battle formation on the Chaizi Kou-Li Jiawo road, with the vanguard at the western end of Yangshan, with the purpose of defending Tongshan. The west army gathered near Lizhuang, about a thousand meters east of the western end of Dagu Mountain, before 8:00 AM, advancing to occupy the position before the battle, with the purpose of attacking Tongshan from Dangshan. The two sides formed a confrontational situation. In order to make it easier for the main force to defeat and drive away the invading enemy, the east army advanced westward north of Jiulishan with a mixed regiment, cutting off the Bian-Xu transportation and forcing the left flank of the west army. At the same time, the west army also occupied positions in the Zhengzhuang, Dagu Mountain, and Qilihe area with a mixed regiment, transferring the offensive at the opportunity. The two sides advanced and attacked each other. At about 3:00 PM in the afternoon, the two armies engaged in a decisive battle at Jiantun, Guishan, and Xiaogu Mountain, which was then completed. During the decisive battle, the soldiers in the front line of the two armies were only about a hundred meters apart, and the two regimental commanders ordered the exercise to stop. The chief judges of the two armies marched and judged along with the troops. Zhu, Wang Jun, and visitors climbed to the peak of Jiulishan to observe the battle. After the exercise, Zhu announced that the review of the various subjects of the Seventh Division had been completed and scheduled a gathering for review and instruction on the morning of the (26th). He will then go west that day. (25th)

The Course of the Qingdao Local Produce Merchants' Strike 75

Qingdao dispatch: The strike of local produce merchants in Qingdao is now expanding and becoming a serious problem. If this matter is not resolved one day, the entire city's commerce will be affected. The cause of the strike and the mediation efforts of the party and government authorities are detailed below:

Causes of the Strike: On the first of last month, the guild of cargo companies telegraphed the Ministry of Industry of the Executive Yuan, requesting cancellation of the fact that peanuts and oil shipped to China also had to be inspected and charged before they could be shipped, as it was too harsh. Soon, an telegram was received from the Ministry of Industry, which stated roughly that in consideration of the merchants' difficulties, the Qingdao Commodity Inspection Bureau had been ordered to exempt all non-foreign commodities from inspection fees, except for cotton that had been thoroughly inspected and commodities specially approved by the ministry due to special circumstances. At the same time, the Commodity Inspection Bureau also issued an announcement in accordance with the order, stipulating that free of charge would be implemented first on the 23rd, and the items that should be excluded would be stipulated by the ministry. Not long after, the bureau sent a letter to the Chamber of Commerce, stating that according to the Ministry of Industry's telegram, peanuts and oil in the commodities were prone to mold and often mixed with impurities, which were related to food. Regardless of whether they were exported or sold domestically, they still had to be inspected and charged. Upon hearing the news, the local produce merchants immediately wrote to the bureau, stating that the goods sold by various companies in the past few days were all in Da Wen Kou, Jinan, etc. Now that they have received the notice, they still have to pay inspection fees. However, domestic transportation is delayed, making it difficult to catch up. They are now requesting exemption from the ministry, and they are still willing to refer to free of charge within these three weeks. At the same time, they wrote to the Ministry of Industry again, stating that Qingdao's local products include several types, which have all been generously exempted from inspection fees. However, only peanuts and oil, which are related to the people's livelihood and daily necessities, have resumed inspection fees, which is unfair. Unexpectedly, the Ministry of Industry's approval did not arrive, and the Inspection Bureau issued another announcement on the 13th, stating that according to the Ministry of Industry's telegram, the request for a three-week postponement of the inspection fees for peanuts should be approved, and the Ministry of Industry's telegram should still be followed upon expiration. It also stated that the fees would be implemented on the 16th, expiring on March 14th. The local produce merchants were extremely frightened because they had not received the ministry's approval and the bureau suddenly announced the imposition of fees. They requested the bureau to postpone it again, but the bureau refused, and the strike broke out as a result.

Focus of the Dispute: The Inspection Bureau's side believes that peanuts and oil are Qingdao's only major export, and tens of thousands of yuan in fees can be collected annually. The bureau's expenses depend entirely on this income. If these two items are once exempted from fees, the bureau will be unable to support itself. Therefore, the local produce merchants believe that first, the bureau's fees are too high (five cents per picul for peanuts and nine cents per picul for peanut oil), second, there are many procedures for inspection, obtaining tickets, and paying fees, which require more partners, third, waiting for inspection often delays shipping schedules and suffers losses due to market price fluctuations, and fourth, inspection bureaus everywhere do not inspect or charge fees for goods sold domestically. It is unfair for Qingdao to do so alone. Therefore, they also firmly oppose it and will not stop until they achieve their goal.

Mediation Situation: After the local produce merchants went on strike, important figures from the party and government went to the Inspection Bureau to discuss mediation methods with Director Mou Junde. The bureau has replied to the municipal government that starting from the 23rd, peanuts and oil sold domestically will still be reported for inspection, but fees will be temporarily waived, and they will wait for the Ministry of Industry to approve and handle it. However, the local produce merchants' attitude is still extremely firm and they refuse to report for inspection. Also, when the party and government authorities were mediating, the bureau stated that without inspection, the customs would not allow release, and they still had to ask the Ministry of Finance for instructions. The local produce merchants then elected representatives to go to the customs and meet with the tax commissioner to inquire about the matter. The tax commissioner stated that regarding goods sold overseas, according to the ministry's order, they are not allowed to be exported without an inspection certificate. As for goods sold domestically, if the Inspection Bureau sends a letter explaining the situation, the customs can release them. The representatives then went to the bureau yesterday to meet with the director, explained the process of contacting the customs, and asked the director to send a letter to the customs to allow release. The director replied that this matter is being implemented in accordance with the order of the Ministry of Industry, and he does not have the authority to dare to obey the order. This negotiation has still yielded no results. (March 25th)

Central Committee Member Gui Chongji Comes to Wuhu for Inspection 76

Wuhu dispatch: Central Committee Member Gui Chongji came to Anhui to inspect the party affairs of the entire province of Anhui. He first went to Anqing from Nanjing and stayed for about two weeks. A few days ago, he took the Anfeng charter boat from Anqing to Datong for inspection and stayed in Tong for three days. Today (24th) at 5:00 PM, he took the boat back to Wuhu. All sectors of the Wuhu party and government welcomed him at the Jianggan Pier. Gui and his entourage, including Xiao Fengwei and Qiu Zhanwu, secretaries of the Central Propaganda Department, got off the boat and went to the Southeast Hotel on Zhongshan Road to rest. Then, they met with reporters from local newspapers and announced the situation of the inspection of party affairs in Anhui Province, roughly stating that since the reorganization of party affairs in Anhui, the organization has indeed become more rigorous and the work has also made considerable progress. However, although mass organizations have been reorganized and established one after another, I am not clear about the goals of their own work, which is a common problem of mass organizations. I hope to pay attention to this. It is reported that Gui will stay in Wuhu for about four or five days and then transfer to Hefei. After inspecting in Hefei for three days, he will return to Wuhu and take the road back to Nanjing. Accompanying staff will be sent to Xuan City, Fanchang, and other counties for inspection. (24th)

High Ying's Appeal Case Argument Concludes 77

Verdict Scheduled for the 30th of This Month

Former San Francisco Vice Consul Gao Ying, his wife Liao Suqiu, and Chief Clerk Sun Yuan were apprehended by US customs officials for trafficking opium. They were extradited back to China, and after first and second trials by the Jiangning Local Court and the Jiangsu Higher Court, Gao Ying was sentenced to six years of imprisonment and a fine of six thousand yuan for opium trafficking and attempted bribery. Sun Yuan was sentenced to five years of imprisonment and a fine of five thousand yuan. Liao Suqiu was sentenced to four years of imprisonment and a fine of four thousand yuan. Each of them appealed to the Supreme Court, which, on October 6th of last year, rejected the appeal of Gao and Liao, but remanded the cases of Gao Ying and Sun Yuan for a new trial. Today (the 26th), at 2:00 PM, the Jiangsu Higher Court's Criminal Division Presiding Judge Lin Dawen, Judges Lin Zhezhang and Zhang Bingci, Prosecutor Zhu Wenzhuo, and Clerk Liu Suize convened the trial. Gao and Liao have been seriously ill recently and were originally unable to attend the court. However, due to their crucial involvement in the case, a cardiotonic injection was administered by the prison doctor, Ruan Jiemin, at 12:00 AM in the prison, and they were reluctantly carried to the High Court in rattan chairs. Of the witnesses summoned, one was Chen Yiyi, the former Mexican Consul who had already completed his term and been released, and the other was Gong Anqing, the former San Francisco Consul General. However, neither Chen nor Gong reported for duty. Chen Yiyi had already left for Japan on the 18th of this month to seek employment, and his wife, Chen Yang Wenbin, reported in his place. After the court convened, Gao Ying's lawyers, Wang Youling and Liu Shifang, and Sun Yuan's lawyers, Li Zongqian and Lu Jianai, appeared in court together. They announced the conclusion of the argument in court, and the verdict was scheduled for 1:00 PM on the 30th of this month. The details of the court hearing are recorded as follows:

The court convened at 2:00 PM. First, Gao Ying was questioned. The judge asked his age, and he replied thirty-six years old. Asked where he was from, he replied Fujian. Asked his occupation, he replied that he was formerly the Vice Consul at the Chinese Consulate in San Francisco. Asked that the Jiangning Local Court sentenced you for helping to smuggle opium, and you appealed, and later you still refused to accept it and appealed again, and the Supreme Court sent it back for retrial. Could you please state your reasons for the appeal again? He replied that because he was completely unaware of the opium smuggling matter beforehand and did not conspire, he disagreed with the verdict. As for the dereliction of duty, although Chen Yiyi had sent a letter requesting assistance, he did not agree. His reasons for the appeal were as such.

Sun Yuan was then questioned. Asked his age, he replied forty-one years old. Asked where he was from, he replied Zhongshan, Guangdong. Asked his occupation, he replied that he was a chief clerk at the Chinese Consulate in San Francisco. Asked if he had previously been the secretary of the consulate, he replied yes, before September of the 17th year of the Republic. Asked who arrived at the consulate first, Gao Ying or himself, he replied that he arrived first. Asked how many chief clerks were at the San Francisco Consulate, he replied one. Asked if the consulate should send someone to pick up Chinese people arriving in the United States, he replied not necessarily, only if there was a notification. Asked if Gao Ying and Gao Liao Suqiu arrived in the United States at the same time, he replied yes. Asked how many times Liao Suqiu had returned to China, he replied two or three times, somewhat vague, he couldn't remember. Asked if he knew Wen Yuxian Shen Guang, he replied that he did not. Asked that Wen Yuxian sent him a letter, if he did not know him, why would he give him a letter, he replied that he did not see Wen Yuxian's letter, or it was fabricated. Asked if he had ever seen this letter, he replied that he only saw it in court later. Asked that Wen Yuxian asked Gao Liao Suqiu in his letter, "Please trouble brother to open the overseas box personally, check the numbers and transfer them," since he did not recognize him, it would have been better to directly hand it over to Gao Liao Suqiu, why hand it over to him to transfer, he replied that he really did not know. Asked that the letter said to hand over number two and number eleven to Shou Nan, and the rest to Ruo Yun, then did he recognize Shou Nan and Ruo Yun, he replied that he did not recognize either of them. Asked that there were a total of two thousand two hundred and ninety-nine cans of opium, and he stated the prices and numbers very clearly in the letter, since he did not recognize him, why was it so clear, he replied that this needed to be asked of the person carrying it. Asked since he did not recognize the person, how would he transfer the goods, he replied that he could not transfer the goods if he did not recognize the person. Asked if Wen Yuxian had sent a letter before Gao Liao Suqiu returned to the United States, he replied no. Asked when Gao Liao Suqiu arrived in San Francisco, he replied July 5th. Asked how he knew, he replied that Gao Ying told him that his wife was coming back soon. Asked if there were any other words, he replied no. Asked if Gao Ying went to pick her up when Gao Liao Suqiu arrived at the dock, he replied that he did not go because Consul General Gong was not there. Asked if he went to be questioned by the Americans after the incident, he replied that he went to turn himself in because it involved him. Asked according to his statement, then he had not contacted beforehand, he replied yes.

Gao Ying was questioned again. Asked if he had another name called Jiande, he replied yes, it was his courtesy name. Asked when he arrived in San Francisco, he replied May of the 14th year. Asked if Liao Suqiu was his wife, he replied yes. Asked how many times Gao Liao Suqiu had returned to China, he replied three times. Asked when was the most recent time, he replied January 4th of the 18th year of the Republic. Asked when she returned to the United States, he replied July 5th. Asked why she returned to China, he replied because she was not feeling well, and she returned to the country with friends and relatives. Asked if he knew Wen Yuxian Shen Guang, he replied that he did not know. Asked if Gao Liao Suqiu had told him about bringing opium, he replied no. Asked if he had received a letter beforehand, he replied yes, he said he was coming back on the Tenyo Maru. Asked if this letter was still kept, he replied that it was lost. Asked how he knew that Gao Liao Suqiu was carrying opium, he replied that because the luggage was detained, he went to the customs to check, and the people at the customs told him so. Asked if he later sent a telegram asking Minister Wu to intercede, he replied yes, when drafting the telegram, he only

Page 8

knew it was a small amount and did not know it was opium. Asked since he did not know beforehand, why did he say in the telegram to Minister Wu, "My wife is returning on the Tenyo, there are a few drugs in the boxes, brought by my wife under the instigation of others," etc., he replied that after Gao Liao Suqiu returned, he asked her, and she said that Chen Sheng asked her to bring the luggage, and he thought this was inappropriate, and the tax officer's words must have a basis, so he guessed that she was being instigated by others. Asked if the letter did not have Chen Sheng's name, only writing that the shipper was Wen Yuxian Shen Guang, was this Chen Sheng a fake name, he replied that he did not know at all. Asked if he went when the boxes were opened, he replied that he was not present when his three pieces of luggage were opened. Asked that the sender was Shen Guang Wen Yuxian, the deliverer was Sun Yuan, and the recipients were Shou Nan Ruo Yun, since the case had been discovered, why did he not investigate, he replied that the American judicial system was different from China's, and the letter was not published. Asked that he did not know Shou Nan Ruo Yun in the United States, he replied that most people in San Francisco were from Guangdong, and he rarely associated with those people. Asked if the diplomatic seal and consulate signature were given to Gao Liao Suqiu by him, he replied no, the consulate did not have signatures and diplomatic seals. Asked if he sent a telegram to Minister Wu asking the customs to waive inspection, whether to take the opium back, he replied no, because if opium was found during the inspection, it would be related to the national dignity, so he thought if the inspection was waived, then the luggage would be returned.

The judge then questioned about the dereliction of duty. Asked if he knew Chen Yiyi, he replied yes, he was the Mexican Vice Consul. Asked when Mei Guang and four others arrived in the United States, and when Chen Yiyi wrote a letter to him, he replied around May of the 17th year, and then another letter came ten days later, asking him to agree, which was enough to prove that he did not collude. At that time, after he received the letter in the United States, he immediately refused because the United States paid great attention to the landing of overseas Chinese, and they must have a passport from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. Since he earnestly requested it, then this passport was probably not formal. In the second letter, he said that if there was no reply in a month, he would call them to the United States. At that time, he immediately replied to him, probably he did not receive his letter because the postal route from China to the United States took twenty-one to twenty-three days. Regarding this matter, he repeatedly telegraphed him for assistance, but he never agreed. Asked if he had ever asked the Consul General for Chen Yiyi, he replied that because Chen Yiyi did say so in the telegram, he had reported the situation to the Consul General. Asked when Mei Guang and four others arrived in San Francisco, he replied June 8th. Asked if he had ever been on their ship, he replied that because Chen Yiyi had asked him, he went specifically to tell the immigration bureau to check their passports, and if they were forged, they should be detained. Asked if he took it back after the passport was found to be forged, he replied yes.

Sun Yuan was questioned again. Asked if Gao Ying went to the ship after Mei Guang and four others arrived in the United States, he replied yes. Asked him to describe what happened, he replied that after Gao Ying went to the ship, he returned to report to the Consul General, saying that four Chinese people were using fake passports. The Consul General then told him, "You go check again." After he went to check, the situation was the same as what Gao Ying said. Gao Ying took the passports.

Then Gao Liao Suqiu was questioned. Ms. Liao's health was deteriorating, and she was supported to the court by bailiffs. When asked her name and age, she nodded to indicate. The judge asked if she went to San Francisco with Gao Ying, and she replied yes. Asked if the boxes were entrusted to be carried, she replied that Chen Sheng did it, and they were handed over to her in Guangdong. Asked what was inside, she replied that she did not know. Asked if the diplomatic seal and the consulate signature were given to her by Gao Ying, she replied no. Asked where they came from, she replied to ask people from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. Asked if the two letters in the box were from Sun Yuan, Shou Nan and Ruo Yun, did she recognize these two people, she replied no. Asked if she had told Gao Ying about the things in the box, she replied no. Asked if she was not detained after arriving in San Francisco on July 5th, she replied yes, she went home immediately, and later went to the countryside to see the children and came back on the eighth. Asked since she did not tell her husband, how did her husband know that she was being instigated by others to smuggle drugs, she replied that after being detained by customs, her husband asked her, and she said that Chen Sheng asked her to bring luggage, and she feared that there were toxic substances inside. Asked if she had written to Gao Ying before going to San Francisco, she replied yes, only to ask him to pick her up. At this point, the judge asked Gao Ying again, did Liao Suqiu go to the countryside immediately after arriving in San Francisco, he replied yes, because there was still a child in the countryside.

Finally, Chen Yiyi's wife, Yang Wenbin, was questioned. Yang supplied that she was thirty-two years old, from Huangni Bridge, Wuxi. Asked why her husband did not come, she replied that since he was implicated in the criminal case, he went to Japan on the 18th to earn a living because he had no means of livelihood. Asked if she was representing him in court today, she replied yes, because the court summoned her husband, and she dared not not come. Asked if she was summoned today because she was a witness in Gao Ying's attempt to bribe, she replied that her husband did not know. After the questioning, Prosecutor Zhu stood up to argue, followed by Lawyer Wang and others who stood up to argue one after another. The court announced the conclusion of the argument and scheduled the verdict for the 30th of this month.

Wuxi 81

Police Officer Commits Suicide by Shooting Chen Desheng, a police officer of the Second Squad of the Second Company of the County Police Brigade, was 23 years old, originally from Zhejiang, and had served as a police officer in the 14th Public Security Bureau. He was discharged in December last year and immediately filled the position of officer in the squad. He was diligent in his service on weekdays. Unexpectedly, at 6:00 AM yesterday morning, he suddenly pointed a box cannon at his chest in the dormitory and pulled the trigger, immediately falling to the ground and dying. The police officers in the same team were greatly frightened and ran to report to Captain Wang, who reported it to the County Court. Prosecutor Zhu Zonghai was dispatched to conduct an inspection and confirmed that it was a suicide by shooting. The team prepared a coffin for burial. There are various opinions on the cause of suicide, and it cannot be determined.

Three Suspected Thieves Apprehended On the night of the day before yesterday, at around 11:00 PM, in the former deserted graves in Chenxiang Village, 4th District (Kaiyuan Township) of the county, bandits were lurking there and using flashlights to shine into the grave area. Longevity Boat Robbed The Longevity Township's Huang Panquan's boat, on the 24th, carrying two passengers, one of whom was a cloth shop clerk carrying forty bolts of twill fabric and two hundred yuan in cash, and another twenty bolts of twill fabric and two hundred yuan in cash, was intercepted by a pirate ship while sailing to Qianmu Bridge in Huangtang. Ten Direction Chan Temple Monks Dispute The Ten Direction Chan Temple in Nanwai is a famous Chan forest in Jiangyin. Recently, the host monk Zuo Yu and the hermitage monk Yuelang have been in litigation with each other over the position of abbot. Gong Xin of Huashu, the owner of the hermitage, stated that the hermitage was founded with donations from the Ming dynasty investigator-general, Xiu Ling, specifically for the elderly monks of the ten directions to practice and cultivate. Traditionally, the abbot must submit the annual accounts to the Gong family for review every year. In recent years, they have suddenly stopped submitting the accounts for review and have also had disputes, which has betrayed the original intention of the ancestor who founded the hermitage. Yesterday, he invited Shen Songshou, the district head of the 9th district, to visit Magistrate Li and strictly rectify the rules of the hermitage in order to extend its longevity.

Catching Knife Fish Leads to Homicide Shi Molang, who lives by the Wangjia Chensan Dyke in the second district of Danan Township, makes a living by fishing. On the morning of the day before yesterday (21st), he and Yu Xiaobao, from the village in front of Maixi Dyke, Wushan Port, were catching knife fish. The two sides quarreled over the location for catching fish. Accidentally, he hit Xiaobao on the head with a stick, and he died in less than half a day. Subsequently, the township head Lu Shengbing and others mediated, ordering Shi to pay one hundred and eighty yuan to cover the cost of the coffin, etc., in order to settle the matter. However, because the family of the deceased did not agree, they carried the coffin into Shi's house and destroyed the furniture. His younger brother, Xiaobao, was twisted and imprisoned in the defense corps for three days, and was sent to the county for interrogation on the 25th.

Hangzhou 86

Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway Trial Run Yesterday The track laying project of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway has recently advanced to Jianshan. Three 260-model Gul locomotives purchased this year from De Arensden Koebel Factory have also been assembled. Yesterday, the chief of the locomotive section of the bureau led all the staff to conduct a trial run, making one round trip from the riverside to Xiaoshan, covering a distance of about 18 kilometers. The car body was unusually stable and comfortable, and the result was quite satisfactory.

Municipal Government Plans to Dredge West Lake The Hangzhou Municipal Government believes that the siltation of West Lake has become increasingly serious in recent years, which is not only related to the scenery but also affects farmland. It has specially planned fundamental dredging methods, first blocking and building bridge holes in Su and Bai causeways, building four earthen dams, using water pumps to pump dry the accumulated water, and requisitioning 3,500 civilian workers to excavate the silt. The area of dredged mud is about 2,149,500 square meters, and the standard is to deepen the exposed lake surface by 50 centimeters. It is estimated that 645,000 cubic meters of earth will be excavated to fill the low-lying areas of the entire lake. The total cost is estimated at 200,000 yuan. Mayor Chen believes that the project is large and expensive, and the provincial treasury is short of funds, making it difficult to implement. Yesterday, he ordered the Public Works Bureau to re-reduce the audit so that the cost is lighter and easier to undertake, and construction can start immediately.

Important News

Sino-Japanese Cultural Agreement 88

Our Country Has Decided to Revoke It

The Japanese Side Has Been Notified by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs

According to reliable sources from the Central News Agency, the Sino-Japanese Cultural Agreement is a one-sided treaty. The Japanese side has always relied on this agreement as a tool for cultural aggression against our country. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs, based on a letter from the Ministry of Education, has repeatedly instructed Ambassador Wang Rongbao in Japan to negotiate with the Japanese side to abolish it. For more than a year, it has been heard that the Japanese side has consistently refused to agree. Now, our country has decided to revoke the agreement, and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs will notify the Japanese side of this decision.

Primary and Secondary Schools Should Emphasize Labor Work and Production Operations 89

The Ministry of Education issued a circular to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities, instructing primary and secondary schools to increase work courses, vocational training, and labor operations, and to report the progress of implementation for review and approval. The circular stated, "It has been found that primary and secondary school education in our country has not paid enough attention to labor work and production operations. Therefore, graduates of various schools are generally unable to work hard or engage in labor, and have no ability to engage in vocational production. At a time when production is declining and people's livelihood is withering, school education cannot adapt to the needs of society to seek remedies, but instead cultivates a large number of young people who have higher desires and specialize in dividing benefits, resulting in graduates who have no skills to support themselves and earn a living, which is not only useless to society, but also has an impact that will make society more unstable. This is a past shortcoming in education that we should strive to correct. The educational purpose of the Republic of China promulgated by the central government has three major points: "enriching the people's lives, supporting social survival, and developing the people's livelihood." Within the implementation guidelines, it is further stipulated that "general education must be based on the teachings of Premier Sun Yat-sen, and ... cultivate the people's lives and increase the people's production capacity as the main purpose," etc., which are meant to remedy deficiencies and have good intentions. All our educational institutions should adhere to and comply with them and not allow them to be overlooked. In order to implement this educational purpose and remedy the shortcomings of education, the specific matters that should be done and handled are listed below: (1) Public and private primary schools must strictly implement the work courses as stipulated in the temporary standards of the primary school curriculum promulgated by the ministry; (2) Public and private junior high schools must strictly comply with the agriculture, industry, and home economics courses as stipulated in the temporary standards of the junior high school curriculum promulgated by the ministry, and carefully comply with them in light of local conditions; (3) Public and private primary and secondary school students must participate in labor work within the school, and special attention should be paid to production operations in each subject; (4) When provincial, municipal, and county supervisors conduct inspections, they should pay special attention to the results of agriculture, industry, home economics, and other subjects (5) The department should carry out propaganda and promotion for labor production education in many ways, so that society and families can understand the current trend of our country. All the above points should be supervised and complied with separately. If the equipment is insufficient and teachers are difficult to obtain, funds should be increased within a limited time to enrich the content, and teachers should be trained in many ways within the scope of the department in charge in order to achieve practical results. The progress of the handling should be prepared and checked. This order.

Ministry Order on Mongolian and Tibetan Areas Preparing Social Education 90

The Ministry of Education orders the various banners and chiefs of Mongolia and Tibet to swiftly prepare for public education, such as literacy campaigns, public schools, public libraries, public reading rooms, and popular lecture halls, etc., in order to popularize education in the border regions. The detailed outlines for public school measures and the literacy campaign propaganda plan are also issued, and they are to be followed accordingly. The order states: "Upon investigation, social education in our country has made considerable progress in the inland provinces in recent years. However, Mongolia and Tibet are located in remote border areas with backward cultures, and social education is still in its infancy. In order to promote education in these border regions, in addition to vigorously promoting and expanding Mongolian and Tibetan school education, special attention should also be paid to social education in Mongolia and Tibet. The main facilities for social education are literacy campaigns, public schools, public education centers, public libraries, public reading rooms, and popular lecture halls, etc. These organizations are simpler than all the facilities of school education and are also easier to prepare. Therefore, a special order is issued to the banners and chiefs to follow this instruction, quickly set up the above-mentioned important social education institutions as appropriate, so that the general public can have opportunities to seek knowledge, and border education can be gradually developed. This is of utmost importance." The detailed outlines for public school measures and the literacy campaign propaganda plan are also issued, and they are to be followed accordingly. (

(Detailed outlines for public school measures and literacy campaign propaganda plan are omitted for now)

Zhejiang Province Consolidated Tax Abolished; Education Funds to be Collected 91

Pending the Opening of Business Tax Collection

Education Department Instructs Various Counties

Previously, the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Education received a report from the Haiyan County Government stating that various education funds collected under the consolidated tax had been abolished, making it impossible to compensate for the losses. It requested that the Finance Department be consulted to allocate the funds in the same amount when the business tax was implemented. The Department of Education believed that this situation was not unique to Haiyan County. After investigation, other counties and cities should also be handled in the same way regarding the education funding that should be allocated to compensate for the abolition of the Likin tax. Furthermore, the Provincial Government Committee had previously resolved at its 380th meeting to instruct the Department of Education to jointly investigate with the Finance Department to determine the exact amount and negotiate for allocation. However, the investigation and reply for this case would take time, and the counties and cities urgently needed the aforementioned education funding. It was inconvenient to suspend it because of this. It was proposed to forward the matter to the Finance Department for investigation and to instruct the current business tax bureaus in various districts to allocate the funds as soon as they are collected and forward them to the county and city governments for emergency use. In the meantime, the Department of Education would wait for the counties and cities to report completely and then negotiate with the Finance Department to make an overall allocation and submit it to the Provincial Government for approval. The Finance Department replied that the education funding that had been allocated from the consolidated tax surtax was now without resources due to the abolition of the Likin tax. Since the Provincial Government Committee had resolved to investigate the amount and allocate it, it should be handled accordingly. As soon as the business tax is implemented, separate orders will be issued to comply. The Finance Department also informed the Department of Education for review. The Department of Education specifically informed Haiyan County yesterday and separately instructed the county and city governments to instruct their subordinate education bureaus and the education fund association, and also forwarded the information to the local business tax bureaus.

Shandong Province Vigorously Implements Public Education 92

Jinan Telegram, He Siyuan, Director of the Shandong Provincial Department of Education, plans to have public schools attached to various agencies and schools at the provincial, municipal, and county levels in order to vigorously implement public education throughout the province. Today (the 24th), the 44th regular meeting of the Provincial Government approved its provisional regulations and supplementary measures. The following is a transcript: "Supplementary Measures to the Provisional Regulations for Public Schools Attached to Various Agencies in Shandong Province" (1) Public schools attached to various agencies in Shandong Province shall be governed by these measures in addition to the Provisional Regulations for Public Schools Attached to Various Agencies in Shandong Province. (2) The education bureaus of each county and city shall organize a Public School Promotion Committee, the organizational regulations of which shall be determined separately. (3) Administrative agencies with monthly expenses of more than 500 yuan shall have at least one public school attached. Those with less than 500 yuan may be jointly established by two or three agencies. (4) Schools at all levels, vocational teachers, or staff of educational agencies with three or more people shall have one public school attached. (5) Temples, guild halls, charitable organizations, or other groups that exist with legal permission and have fixed assets or regular expenses shall be supervised by the county and city governments along with the education bureaus to urge them to report the dates separately to the Department of Education for record. (7) The performance of various agencies and schools in running public schools may be listed as one of the administrative performance indicators. (8) Each public school shall be under the guidance of the highest local educational administrative agency. (9) All start-up and recurring expenses for public schools attached to various agencies and schools shall be paid from the budget of each agency and school. (10) These measures shall be implemented from the date of their approval and promulgation.

Second Annual Meeting of the China Child Education Society 100

The China Child Education Society is the only organization in China that studies child education. Since its establishment, it has been in existence for four years. There are now more than 30 group members and more than 400 individual members. It publishes a monthly journal of child education, which is published by Shanghai Kaiming Bookstore. Its content discusses family education, kindergarten education, and elementary school education, and is highly praised by the education community. The society will hold its second annual meeting at the Public Works Bureau North District Elementary School on Kenenhai Road, Shanghai, for three days from April 16 to 19 and 20. Everything is now being prepared. Members attending the meeting must report to the Annual Meeting Office at No. 20 Museum Road, Shanghai, on the 70th to receive printed materials. Municipal Party Department Prepares to Commemorate Huanghuagang Martyrs 115

Measures Have Been Drafted

Meeting to be Held on the 29th Morning

In the year before the founding of the Republic, after the failure of the Guangzhou New Army Uprising, the Kuomintang decided to try again. Dr. Sun Yat-sen, the Premier of the Kuomintang, convened Huang Xing, Hu Hanmin, Zhao Boxian, and others at the British-owned Penang for a secret meeting. It was decided to mobilize the elite of the entire party to make a desperate move. The date of the uprising was originally set for March 15, but later it was postponed to the 29th due to the fact that the military equipment and funds were not fully equipped, and the stricter precautions taken by the Qing officials due to the Wen Shengcai assassination of Fu Qi. Huang Xing arrived in the province in advance, and the comrades who were going to die gathered together. After a meeting, they wrapped white cloth around their arms, carried sharp weapons, and rushed to the Liangguang Governor's Office. It was 5:30 PM on March 29 of the Xinhai year. Although the Qing officials were prepared, they failed. However, the heroic spirit of the 72 martyrs of Huanghuagang, who fought with iron and blood and were the pioneers of the people, was enough to wake up the Chinese people and save the nation from disaster. The spread of revolutionary ideas throughout the country and the success of the Xinhai Revolution in one fell swoop were due to the merits of the martyrs of Huanghuagang. The Propaganda Department of the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department has drafted commemorative measures and submitted them to the Municipal Executive Committee for deliberation. The measures have now been fully approved. The following is an excerpt:

Commemoration aspects (1) At 9:00 AM on March 29, party departments at all levels, agencies, and groups shall send four representatives to the third floor of the Municipal Party Department to hold a commemorative meeting. (2) Agencies, groups, and schools may hold commemorative meetings separately. (3) Districts far from the city, such as Jiangwan, Wusong, Pudong, Zhenru, and Meilong, may hold commemorative meetings separately. (4) The Municipal Party Department shall notify all circles in the city: (1) all flags in the city shall be flown at half-mast for one day, (2) banquets and entertainment shall be suspended for one day, (3) all citizens shall wear black gauze on their arms for one day, (4) all trams and buses in the city shall fly flags at half-mast for one day, (5) the entire city shall have a holiday for one day.

Propaganda aspects (1) Main propaganda points: (1) based on the commemorative methods for revolutionary memorial days, (2) based on the propaganda outline issued by the central government. (2) Propaganda materials: (1) leaflets, (2) slogans, (3) a letter to compatriots and comrades, (4) a special issue of Party Voice, (5) special commemorative issues published in various districts, (6) commemorative albums, (7) major newspapers publish portraits of martyrs and publish special issues. (3) Propaganda methods: (1) permanent propaganda teams from various district branches set off for propaganda, (2) posters are posted, (3) leaflets are distributed.

New Director of the Foreign Affairs Office, Tang Liu, Took Office Yesterday 117

Expressing His Willingness to Be Close to the Press

Tang Liu, the newly appointed director of the Foreign Affairs Office in Shanghai, assumed his post at the office at 11:00 AM yesterday. The details are as follows:

Tang Liu's Remarks: When Director Tang arrived, the former deputy director, Liu Yunfang, happened to be present as well. As the two were old acquaintances, they went to the director's office for a pleasant chat, during which they also discussed matters regarding the handover.

Convening a Meeting and Giving Instructions: Subsequently, they went to the reception room and gathered all the staff. Mr. Liu Yunfang introduced them one by one. Director Tang Liu then gave a brief address, generally expressing his hope that all colleagues would work diligently together with one heart and mind.

Handling the Handover: After the address, Director Tang designated staff to handle the inventory process. It is said that the files were quite simple, as the archives of the former Jiangsu Negotiation Office had been transferred to the ministry for safekeeping, so there weren't many files in the office. However, the equipment was relatively complex, and the inventory was not completed yesterday and will continue today.

Taking Over the Discussion Committee: Chen Shiguang, the former director of the secretariat of the Foreign Affairs Discussion Committee of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, did not attend the handover yesterday due to being on vacation. Therefore, Zhao Tiezhang, the section chief of the discussion committee and concurrently the section chief of the office, handled the handover procedures. According to Director Tang, although it wasn't necessary to hold a separate inauguration ceremony for the director of the secretariat of the discussion committee, he had effectively taken over the position at the same time.

Tang's Remarks: Director Tang told reporters from the news agency yesterday that diplomacy relies entirely on public opinion as its backing, and newspapers are the mouthpiece of the people, the means by which public opinion is expressed. He expressed his sincere hope to be in contact with the press at all times in the future, so as to facilitate communication.

Meeting with Reporters: Director Tang has designated that all news to be released during his office hours will be handled by him personally when he is in the office. When he is out on official business, section chief Zhao Tiezhang will take over the reception.

Tang's Biography: Tang Liu, courtesy name Nianci, is 30 years old and from Zhongshan County, Guangdong. He is the son of Mr. Tang Shaoyi. He holds a bachelor's degree from Fudan University in Shanghai. He has served as a chief clerk at the Chinese embassy in the United States, an assistant secretary in the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, a third secretary at the Chinese embassy in the United States, a secretary in the Ministry of Justice, a member of the Communications Research Committee of the Ministry of Communications, a consul in Batang, a consul in Surabaya, an inspector of the Ministry of Communications stationed in Surabaya, a counselor and advisor to the Northeast Border Defense Army, a consul in Nagasaki, a consul-general in Singapore, and a member of the Foreign Affairs Discussion Committee.

The Shanghai-Yichang Direct Flight Route is Officially Scheduled 119

Flights Will Begin on the 31st of This Month

Flying Every Day Except Monday

The Journey Takes Ten Hours

The Hankou-Yichang flight route planned by the China National Aviation Corporation has been completed. The pontoons in Shashi and the radio equipment at the Shayichang Airport have all been installed. The official commencement of flights has been set for the 31st of this month, initially carrying mail and temporarily not carrying passengers. The company has recently decided to dispatch a special plane directly from Shanghai to Yichang to expand its business, passing through eight stops along the way. However, flights will be suspended one day a week on Mondays. The timetable has also been changed. The westbound flight will depart from Shanghai at 7:00 AM every morning, and the eastbound flight will depart from Yichang at 6:00 AM in the morning. Flights from Shanghai to Yichang will be on Tuesdays, Thursdays, and Saturdays, and flights from Yichang back to Shanghai will be on Sundays, Wednesdays and Fridays. The company finalized the flight schedule for the Shanghai-Yichang direct route last night and will send it to the Hankou aviation office this afternoon in preparation for handling it within the next few days. The schedule is as follows: Westbound flight: Shanghai departs at 7:00 AM, arrives in Nanjing at 9:15 AM, departs at 9:30 AM, arrives in Wuhu at 10:05 AM, departs at 10:10 AM, arrives in Anqing at 11:20 AM, departs at 11:25 AM, arrives in Jiujiang at 12:25 PM, departs at 12:40 PM, arrives in Hankou at 2:10 PM, departs at 2:45 PM, arrives in Shashi at 4:15 PM, departs at 4:25 PM, arrives in Yichang at 5:10 PM. In total, the journey from Shanghai to Yichang takes only ten hours and ten minutes. Eastbound flight: Yichang departs at 6:00 AM, arrives in Shashi at 6:40 AM, departs at 6:55 AM, arrives in Hankou at 8:25 AM, departs at 9:00 AM, arrives in Jiujiang at 10:30 AM, departs at 10:45 AM, arrives in Anqing at 11:45 AM, departs at 11:50 AM, arrives in Wuhu at 1:00 PM, departs at 1:05 PM, arrives in Nanjing at 1:40 PM, departs at 1:55 PM, arrives in Shanghai at 4:10 PM. In total, the journey takes ten hours.

Wuxi Silk Industry Opposes Freight Rate Increase 120

Planning to Use Water Transportation for Relief

The Wuxi County Silk Factory Association believes that since the Jinghu, Huhangyong and other routes implemented fare increases, the freight rates have also been increased by 20% at the same time, which has a huge impact on the entire silk industry. Moreover, at the end of last year, various industries, due to the slump in the silk industry, collectively sought relief and reported to the government for approval to issue 8 million yuan in silk industry relief bonds, which will be announced and issued soon to maintain the inherent industry. However, the railway bureau is increasing freight rates at this time, which seems to be contrary to the government's intention to provide relief. From the perspective of silk merchants, they cannot bear the heavy burden any longer. Moreover, when the Yongtailong Transportation Company, which was carrying silk freight cars, had an accident in Shanghai in 1927, the losses of various factories reached nearly 200,000 yuan. Because negotiations with the railway bureau at that time were ineffective, the industry had jointly decided to switch to water transport. Later, the railway bureau sent personnel to mediate and promised to find ways to compensate for the losses within a few years, so the factories abandoned this idea. It has only been three years since then, and suddenly, a price increase is being implemented, which is inconsistent with the previous agreement and not a blessing for merchants. Therefore, the factories held a meeting the day before yesterday and decided to request the railway bureau to waive the increase or give them a special price. Otherwise, in order to take care of their capital, they would have to stop transporting by rail and switch to waterways.

News from the Civil Assembly Election Office 121

Large Numbers of Labor Unions Submit Registration Forms: The Shanghai Municipal Election Office for National Assembly Representatives received registration forms yesterday from more than ten labor unions, including the Postal Workers' Union and the Inland River Shipping Union. The Labor Circle Forms a Proposal Research Association: Comrades in the Shanghai labor circle, considering that the upcoming opening of the National Assembly is of great importance to the future of labor, Hu Shouqi, Chen Peide, Yang Youren, and others initiated the establishment of the Shanghai Labor Circle Proposal Research Association for the National Assembly. Participants include Hou Dachun, Gu Junfeng, Lu Jingshi, Zhou Xuexiang, Gu Yongquan, Li Daofa, and Tao Baichuan. The first meeting was held yesterday at the Municipal Party Headquarters. Civil Servants Can Also Be Elected: Regarding the question of whether civil servants (i.e., current officials) have the right to be elected in the election of National Assembly representatives, Mayor Zhang Yuejun of Shanghai previously telegraphed the central government for interpretation. It is now reported that a reply has been received, stating that civil servants also have the right to be elected, but after being elected, they must suspend their duties and go to Beijing to attend the meeting, and they can only resume their duties after the congress is over.

The City's Farmers' Association Registration Rules Have Been Promulgated 122

The Social Bureau Circulates Orders to All Districts to Comply With Them

The district farmers' associations in the city, which the Social Bureau previously urged to organize, are now being established one after another. All the registration rules of the farmers' associations have been drafted by the Social Bureau and submitted to the municipal government for approval and promulgation, which has been forwarded to the preparatory committees of the farmers' associations in various districts for compliance. The rules are recorded on the left:

Shanghai Municipal Farmers' Association Registration Rules: Article 1: All levels of farmers' associations in the city shall comply with these rules and submit an application to the Social Bureau for registration. Article 2: Anyone initiating the organization of a farmers' association, after obtaining permission from the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department to establish an organizational preparatory committee, shall immediately prepare an application form signed by the initiators, a resume of the preparatory members, and attach the organizational preparatory committee's seal impression form and other documents approved by the Municipal Party Department to the Social Bureau for registration. Article 3: When submitting an application for registration of the preparatory committee for organizing a district farmers' association, in addition to complying with the previous regulations, the following items shall be specified: 1. The estimated number of those qualified to be members of the farmers' association in the area; 2. The names and addresses of those who agree to establish the farmers' association; 3. The names, ages, and addresses of the initiators. Article 4: The farmers' association shall complete its organization within one month after the preparatory committee is registered. After the Municipal Party Department deems it sound, all staff members shall prepare a joint application form, attach the constitution, a list of members, a resume of staff members, and various investigation forms in duplicate, and attach the Municipal Party Department's approval order certifying the soundness of the organization to the Social Bureau for registration. Article 5: The constitution of the farmers' association shall specify the following matters: 1. Name, area, and location of the association; 2. Purpose and mission; 3. Regulations for members' admission, withdrawal, and expulsion; 4. Regulations for the number, authority, term of office, and appointment and dismissal of staff members; 5. Regulations for meetings; 6. Regulations for expenses; 7. Regulations for mutual assistance undertakings; 8. Regulations for changes to the constitution; 9. Regulations for dissolution and liquidation. Article 6: If the farmers' association has not completed its organization and submitted an application for registration within one month after the preparatory committee is registered, the Social Bureau may revoke its registration and ban it. Article 7: After the Social Bureau approves the registration of the farmers' association, it shall immediately issue a registration certificate and a seal and announce it. Article 8: After the farmers' association has been approved for registration, it shall submit all kinds of published printed materials to the Social Bureau for reference at any time, and shall report the following amounts to the Social Bureau for review and filing every year: 1. Staff resume; 2. Changes in membership; 3. Business operating conditions and results; 4. Property conditions and budget settlements. Article 9: If the farmers' association needs to amend its rules and regulations or punish members after registration, it shall report to the Social Bureau for approval and filing at any time before it takes effect. Article 10: In the event of any of the following circumstances after the registration of the farmers' association, the Social Bureau shall be notified ten days in advance for approval and filing: 1. The date of convening the general meeting of members or the general meeting of member representatives; 2. Re-election of staff members; 3. Change of property; 4. Conducting fundraising; 5. Applying for liquidation; 6. Reorganization or dissolution of the group. Article 11: After the farmers' association is reorganized or dissolved, the registration certificate and seal shall be revoked immediately, and the Social Bureau shall announce it. Article 12: The matters handled by the Social Bureau in accordance with the provisions of Articles 7 and 10 above shall be reported to the municipal government for referral to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for filing. Article 13: These rules may be amended at any time if there are any omissions. Article 14: These rules shall be implemented from the date of promulgation by the municipal government.

Funding for Dredging the Suzhou Creek 123

The Municipal Government Approves an Allocation of 100,000 Taels of Silver

Ordered the Finance Bureau to Clear the Payment in Five Years

The Shanghai Wusong River Dredging Committee has sent a letter requesting the Junpu Bureau to undertake the dredging project from the mouth of the Suzhou Creek to the vicinity of Yujidun in order to achieve twice the result with half the effort. However, the required funds are very large and should be raised first for application. The committee submitted a document to the municipal government for approval and allocation. It is now learned that the municipal government believes that the river dredging project is indeed urgent, and the required funds are approved for the allocation of 100,000 taels of silver, with 20,000 taels of silver allocated each year to be cleared in five years. In addition to instructing the committee to be informed, the Finance Bureau has been ordered to comply with the allocation.

The Taxpayers' Association Sent a Letter to the Public Works Bureau Yesterday Requesting That It Not Overestimate Rent for Tax Collection 125

Cannot Bear Any Extra Taxes

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association sent a letter to the Public Works Bureau yesterday regarding the matter of the municipal general tax being levied according to the actual rent. The letter stated: "With respect to the municipal general tax, it should be levied according to the actual rent. We have already sent a letter to your bureau requesting that you strictly comply. We have now received letters from Tongdetang, Zhongdeyuan, Yongchangtai, Juxing Printing Bureau, and other firms stating that each of their firms received a notice from the Public Works Bureau of the Public Concession on December 22nd, arbitrarily increasing the housing tax by more than double. They sent letters protesting, stating that they received a letter from your bureau stating that according to Article 5 of the resolution of the taxpayers' annual meeting, the annual rental amount for the houses at numbers 436, 437, 446, and 447 on Henan Road should be increased from 1,404 yuan each to 3,162 yuan. Your bureau will begin collecting taxes according to the new amount on January 1, 1931. If there are any protesters, they should submit a letter to your bureau's general office for review within 14 days from today. We were shocked and horrified. We have investigated and found that the annual rent for each building of the houses we currently occupy is 1,008 taels of silver (i.e., 84 taels per month). We do not know what basis your bureau has for violating its consistent and fair attitude, ignoring the facts, and arbitrarily setting a harsh precedent, increasing the amount from 1,404 yuan to 3,162 yuan per building, which exceeds our actual rent by more than double. We cannot accept this disregard for the facts and arbitrary increase. The intention of Article 5 of the resolution of the taxpayers' annual meeting is nothing more than to provide relief for self-owned properties, and rent is a matter of fact. This is completely different from the intention of the legislation and cannot be used as an example. We cannot bear this extra tax. Moreover, the construction of houses varies, and the amount of rent varies. It is impossible to generalize. Moreover, the current situation is no different from before, and there is no reason to change the established practice arbitrarily. For this reason, we send this letter in the hope that you will look into the actual situation and handle it according to the established practice, collecting taxes according to the actual rent received, so as to conform to the facts and show fairness. After sending the letter, we received a reply stating that it would be submitted to the valuation committee for review, and that the old amount would be collected temporarily. If the review results require payment according to the new amount, the difference must be paid. We believe that regardless of the review results, we can only pay taxes according to the actual rent paid, and we cannot arbitrarily bear any extra taxes. We are afraid that the bureau may make a biased decision, leading to a bad precedent. For this reason, we send this official letter to your association, requesting that you uphold justice and handle the matter for the public good. Please refer to our previous letter and strictly comply. Thank you."

The Goods Exchange Requests a Ten-Year Extension 132

It Should Be Handled After Similar Businesses Are Merged

Yu Hede, the chairman of the Shanghai Securities and Goods Exchange Co., Ltd., submitted a report to the Executive Yuan stating that the term of establishment is about to expire and requesting approval for a ten-year extension. The Executive Yuan stated that Article 55 of the Exchange Law stipulates that when the law is implemented, if there are two or more exchanges of the same type of business in the same area, they should be merged within three years from the date of implementation. It has been found that the business types of the company are the same as those of other exchanges in the same area. The requested extension of the term should be handled after the merger of the various exchanges of the same type of business. Before the merger, it is approved to temporarily continue operations.

Shanghai Shipping Merchants Safeguard Passenger Safety 136

Continued Request for Troops to Escort Ships

Ever since the Jiangshun Wheel of the China Merchants Bureau experienced the tragic incident of demobilized soldiers and gambling bandits murdering the ship's cook, the Bureau has petitioned the Capital Garrison Headquarters to dispatch military police to be stationed on the ship for protection. The Garrison Headquarters approved this request, stating that the dispatch of military police to the ships should be beyond question. Upon receiving this approval, the various shipping bureaus felt quite uneasy and publicly requested the Shipping Association to telegraph the commander-in-chief and deputy commander again, urging them to quickly dispatch troop detachments to be stationed on the ships to reassure passengers. The China Merchants Bureau also continued to petition the headquarters, recounting the harm caused by gambling bandits on Yangtze River ships, who often commit violence and injure people, causing passengers to fear travel. In contrast, foreign merchants' Yangtze River ships have naval protection, leading to thriving businesses and profits tripled. However, state-run Yangtze River ships, even when requesting troop escort for personnel safety, are not granted permission. It is as if seeking to revitalize the shipping industry and reclaim shipping rights is like climbing a tree to catch a fish. It should be requested that the Garrison Headquarters dispatch special service team soldiers to be stationed on Yangtze River ships to protect passengers. If the Garrison Headquarters has difficulties, then please issue a general order to the garrisons at all ports along the Yangtze River, instructing them to dispatch a platoon of soldiers to the docks to provide protection when Chinese merchant Yangtze River ships arrive at the port. In this way, passengers can be guaranteed safety, and bandits can be deterred, and the shipping industry can have hope of flourishing.

Establishment of a Luggage Carrying Service

There are many gangsters in the Shanghai Pudong area, with so-called thirty-six gangs, specializing in forcibly carrying passengers' luggage at various docks, extorting money. If one is not careful, their luggage is snatched away. The hotel industry in Shanghai has already reported this matter to the Public Security Bureau for investigation and prohibition. Recently, such incidents still occur from time to time. Tang Shaoda and others in Nanshi, who specialize in purchasing tickets and transporting passengers on behalf of customers, have raised funds to organize a luggage carrying service for passengers traveling on various Yangtze River and coastal ships, starting from the Jinliyuan Wharf of the China Merchants Bureau, to prevent passengers from being forcibly robbed and extorted by gangsters. Tang and others have submitted a report to the China Merchants Bureau, requesting permission to undertake this service. The Bureau has investigated and confirmed that this will benefit both the shipping bureau and the passengers, and has approved it, requiring Tang and others to pay a deposit of six thousand yuan and conduct a trial for three months. If successful, a contract will be formally signed.

New Developments in Sino-American Aviation 137

New Addition of Companies

With the increasing number of ships traveling the Sino-American route, the American Max Wheel Company has recently decided to open a new route in Shanghai, from Shanghai across the Pacific Ocean to New York. They have specially prepared ten newly built 10,000-ton giant ships with motor engines to operate in China. The first ship, the Neil Max, is scheduled to make its maiden voyage on May 8. After arriving in Shanghai, one ship will be dispatched to Shanghai every month, specializing in carrying passengers and cargo. The American Mostoshi Yoko company is fully authorized to act as its agent in Shanghai.

New York Express Route

The New York express route newly opened by Dale Yangxing Shipping Company is scheduled to begin operations on April 3. Ships traveling from Shanghai to San Francisco will take the Panama Canal to New York, requiring only thirty-six days, one day faster than the fastest Sino-American ships in Shanghai. After the announcement of this new route, customers have been very enthusiastic about booking export cargo, as it is a regular mail ship and the water freight can avoid the huge cost of the Japanese railway transportation.

Songhu Opens Long-Distance Buses 139

Seven Buses Purchased

Operations Begin on May 1

The area between Shanghai and Songjiang has recently become densely populated with thriving commerce and an increasing number of travelers. In terms of transportation, in addition to the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway passing through the area, there are no other vehicles to connect the two places, making it inconvenient for merchants to travel back and forth. Recently, a merchant named Yin Shisheng has been preparing to open a long-distance bus route between Songjiang and Shanghai, starting from Beiqiao Town in Shanghai, passing through more than ten stations such as Maqiao and Huiqiao, and ending in Songjiang. He has submitted a request to the Shanghai County Construction Bureau, which forwarded it to the Construction Department for approval and filing, and requested that the uneven road surfaces in the areas passed through by Beiqiao and other places be slightly repaired to facilitate driving. After investigating the situation, the Bureau believed that operating long-distance buses would benefit the local citizens and the future development of commerce and immediately approved the request, and drafted operating regulations to achieve perfection. It is now reported that the merchant has purchased seven public buses, and the station buildings in Songjiang and Shanghai are also under construction and will be completed soon. It is scheduled to officially operate on May 1 of this year.

To Help with the Spring Famine in Shaanxi Province

Moreover, both emergency and long-term relief require a large amount of relief funds.
