The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Japanese Chamber of Commerce and Industry in Shanghai yesterday, which reads: "We are writing to inform you that on March 25, we received a letter from the Shanghai Sugar Industry Association stating that our member, Yuan Sheng Sugar Firm, reported that Mitsubishi Company had issued 27 warehouse receipts for 1,200 bags of YP ink and 100 bags of YS ink of Dong Sugar. However, when they went to the warehouse to collect the sugar, Mitsubishi suddenly disregarded its credibility and stopped payment to the warehouse, causing the sugar to fail to be collected. We requested you to negotiate. Our chamber sent a letter to Mitsubishi on the 15th of this month to question them, but a week has passed and we have not received a reply. This shows that the company is clearly in the wrong and has secrets that are difficult to answer, so it simply ignores it. In this situation, we should immediately file a complaint with the Japanese consulate for recovery. However, considering that Mitsubishi Company is also a giant among Japanese merchants in Shanghai, in order to avoid excessive emotional harm and uphold the principle of peaceful resolution, we hereby submit the facts and attach a copy of the original letter to Mitsubishi for your review. We also request that you write to the Japanese Chamber of Commerce and Industry in Shanghai and inform Mitsubishi Company to prioritize credibility and promptly cancel the improper stop-payment action, so that Yuan Sheng can collect the sugar and maintain the long-standing credibility of warehouse receipts. If Mitsubishi still fabricates facts and attempts to conceal its mistakes, and fails to comply, then we request that your chamber, together with the Japanese Chamber of Commerce and Industry, order the two parties to come to the meeting to state their reasons and provide mediation or arbitration to avoid litigation and resolve the dispute." A copy of the letter to Mitsubishi was attached. Based on this, the sugar was paid for and the relevant warehouse receipts were issued, and the bills of exchange were also obtained. With the procedures completed, the goods should be delivered according to the receipts. Now, it is reported that Mitsubishi Company has stopped the payment without any reasonable statement, making the warehouse receipts, which have long been credible in Shanghai's commercial community, lose their effect at once, opening up future disputes in the business community and destroying the good habits of past transactions. Mitsubishi Company has been doing business in Shanghai for many years and should not want to break this precedent. We should therefore copy the letter to your office and ask you to inform Mitsubishi Company to deliver the goods according to the receipts to maintain commercial credit and public relations. We also have local news transferred to the back page."

Sudden Change in Local Weather 146

Extremely Hot the Day Before, Extremely Cold Yesterday

Temperature Difference of Four or Five Months

The weather in this port was very warm for the past few days, no different from May or June. It was even worse the day before yesterday. The temperature on the Fahrenheit thermometer rose to 86 degrees. Pedestrians on the road were all wearing single layers. After nightfall, the north wind was fierce and became increasingly strong. Waking up in the morning, the cold wind felt bone-chilling, and cotton clothing was not enough to keep warm, causing a feeling of shrinking. At around 11 a.m., there was a brief rain shower. The wind was even stronger in the afternoon, resembling the weather of severe winter. The weather differed by about four or five months in two days.

Eight Threatening Letters Extorting 30,000 Yuan 147

Appointment to Meet at the Great World

Arrested on Xizang Road

Lin Mengcai, a native of Ningbo, lives at No. 105 Zha Pu Road and works as a clerk at Yuchang Coal Company on Aido Road. Since July 28 of last year, he has successively received eight threatening letters, extorting 30,000 yuan. Lin ignored them because he did not have the financial resources. The last letter was delivered on the 23rd of this month, ordering him to go to the Republican Hall of the Great World at 2 p.m. that day to negotiate. The person going would hold an umbrella and a shoe box as a sign. If he still ignored them, there would be consequences. Lin then sent all the letters to the Hongkou Police Station for investigation. The police sent several detectives to wait in the Republican Hall. Lin also sent Chen Zufeng to hold an umbrella and a box. Waiting until four o'clock, a person wandered alone in the hall but did not dare to talk to Chen. The detectives secretly instructed Chen to go outside to observe his actions. Chen then left, and the person followed him. The detectives also followed behind. When they reached the vicinity of the Far East Hotel on Xizang Road, the person asked Chen to stop and inquired about something. The detectives immediately surrounded and arrested him before he could speak, and took him to the police station. Under questioning, it was learned that he was a native of Nanjing, named Zeng Jinshou. They then went to Dongyouheng Road, Seward Road, Kunming Road, and Shanbei and other places to arrest his accomplices Rong Jinsheng, Huang Linsheng, Rong He氏, Chen Minghe, Liang Lao四, etc., seizing three handguns, two fake handguns, and eighty-nine bullets. Except for Liang Shangji, who was detained at the Sixth District Public Security Bureau, the remaining people were escorted to the Special District Court yesterday along with the guns and bullets, where they were interrogated by Judge Xiao. The plaintiff, Lin Mengcai, had returned to his hometown, so he did not appear in court. Among the defendants, Chen Minghe was Lin's brother-in-law. According to the police investigation, this case was purely initiated by Chen. Cao, Rong, Huang, etc., all claimed that they were helping others. All the threatening letters were written by a Qin surname who was on the run, and the guns and bullets belonged to Chen A'da. The court ordered the defendants to be returned to custody separately and adjourned the hearing for further investigation.

Tan Mei Sues for Divorce Due to Husband's Unsuitability for Marriage 148

Seeks Alimony Compensation

Husband Previously Divorced Twice

Feng Fengzhu, a native of Guangdong, is 41 years old and teaches in Shanghai. On August 24 of the seventeenth year of the Republic, he married Tan Mei, a woman from Xiangshan, as his wife. Tan is currently 23 years old. The couple's relationship has recently deteriorated. Tan decided to divorce him due to her unsuitability for marriage. She first submitted a request to the Special District District Court for mediation. This Monday, the Civil Court President Ying Shi convened both parties for mediation. As a result, their opinions could not be reconciled, and persuasion was ineffective. Tan Mei then retained lawyer Wu Shaoshan to file a formal lawsuit. Her complaint briefly stated that she was seeking a divorce and claiming for alimony due to her inability to live together and her experience of abuse. It stated that on August 24 of the seventeenth year of the Republic, she married Feng Fengzhu after being introduced by a matchmaker named Lu. At that time, both parties belonged to old-fashioned families, so the husband's character was entirely based on the matchmaker's flowery words, creating a castle in the air. The plaintiff's parents were honest and deeply believed it to be true, thinking that Feng Fengzhu was a scholarly son and his character must be extraordinary, celebrating that their beloved daughter had married a dragon and would not have to worry about her son-in-law in the future. The plaintiff was a weak woman in the boudoir who did not understand worldly affairs. Bound by etiquette, she could not consider it in detail. Unexpectedly, a moment of misjudgment led to eternal regret. After entering the door, she learned that Feng Fengzhu was tyrannical by nature, and his actions were vulgar and difficult to describe. It was difficult to harmonize the zither and the se. Occasionally, if there was a disagreement, he would shout and scold, and even use physical violence, leaving scars on her skin. The plaintiff had been taught from an early age to know both books and etiquette. Seeing that her husband's actions were rebellious and tyrannical, and his various behaviors were unbearable, she attempted suicide three times but was unsuccessful. (Omission) Investigation revealed that Feng Fengzhu had been married twice before and had divorced each time. His personality and behavior were self-evident. He became even more extreme and incited his sixteen-year-old son from his previous marriage, Feng Shaoliang, to abuse and insult the plaintiff in every way, which cannot be described. Whenever the plaintiff argued with him, her mother-in-law, Zhu, would assist him in his evil deeds and cut off her food and clothing. The plaintiff gave birth to a child the year after her marriage, and the expenses for raising the child to this day have been borrowed from her mother's family, allowing her to survive meagerly. Feng Fengzhu has never contributed a word of advice. On December 7 of last year, Feng beat the plaintiff severely again for a trivial matter, causing serious injuries. The plaintiff returned to Ning to recuperate. The mother-in-law took the opportunity to file a false accusation with the local court, accusing the plaintiff's mother of abducting her, but the court found the accusation to be baseless and dismissed the case. Based on the above facts, Feng Fengzhu, as the plaintiff's husband, failed to support his wife and children and colluded with his mother and son to devise poisonous plans to trample on women. There could be nothing more extreme. The relationship between husband and wife was completely broken, and it was inevitable that she would request the court to grant a divorce from Feng Fengzhu. The plaintiff's son is only three years old and should be raised by the plaintiff according to reason. She also requests that the defendant be ordered to pay alimony after the divorce, calculated at ten yuan per month until the plaintiff is sixty years old, totaling 22,200 yuan. The court accepted the complaint and immediately notified the defendant to submit a defense within the statutory period, pending scheduling of a hearing.

Conclusion of the Gaochang Temple Incident 149

Municipal Government Protects Passing Vehicles

Social Affairs Bureau Prevents Incitement of Labor Unrest

Regarding the incident in which Chinese tram workers clashed with naval aviation drivers at the Gaochang Temple location, the Social Security and Public Works Bureau sent personnel to thoroughly investigate the facts and report to the Municipal Government for review. The Municipal Government's instructions and the Social Affairs Bureau Director's conversation with reporters are recorded below.

Municipal Government Instructions: The Municipal Government issued the following instructions to the Public Security, Social Affairs, and Public Works Bureaus yesterday: "The submitted documents have been fully reviewed. We will forward a letter to the Naval First Fleet Command, severely punishing drivers such as Zhang Likang, who refused to purchase tickets and caused the incident. We have also sent a letter to the Garrison Command, reiterating the previous order to strictly prohibit fare evasion in order to maintain traffic. Please inform us accordingly." A copy of the order was forwarded.

Director Pan's Remarks: A reporter from the New Sound News visited Director Pan Gongzhan of the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday and inquired about the Gaochang Temple tram case. The conversation is recorded as follows: (Q) How is the conflict between the Chinese tram workers and the naval aviation drivers being handled? (A) This bureau has received instructions from the Municipal Government to investigate thoroughly with the Public Security and Public Works Bureaus and will report the findings to the Municipal Government for review. Now, we have received instructions from the Municipal Government, which has forwarded a letter to the Naval First Fleet Command, severely punishing drivers such as Zhang Likang, who refused to purchase tickets and caused the incident. The Garrison Command has also been requested to reiterate the previous order to strictly prohibit fare evasion, and the Public Security Bureau has been ordered to effectively protect trams passing along that route in order to maintain traffic. (Q) It is rumored that Chinese tram workers will have a second strike because the murderer has not been caught. Has your bureau heard of this? (A) We have not heard of it yet. However, the government has properly planned post-incident management, and we believe that the union members will not take any further excessive actions. If it is confirmed that a small number of troublemakers are taking the opportunity to incite unrest, they will be strictly investigated and dealt with.

Straight Road to Be Built in the Eastern Section of Xiangyin Road in the City Center 150

Construction to Begin Next Month

Asphalt Road to Be Paved at the Same Time

Xiangyin Road, which has been built in the central area of ​​Shanghai, is one of the largest and most important arterial roads. In the future, the Greater Shanghai Plan will be fully realized, the city will gradually prosper, and vehicles wishing to go directly to Wusong will have to pass through this arterial road as the only shortcut outside the concession. The road extends from the West Sports Association Road in the west to the Qiujiang Bridge north of the Jun Gong Road in the east, and the central area is close to the site of the new municipal government. However, the area from Hongbang to Qiujiang Bridge north of Jun Gong Road is an arc-shaped bend. The Municipal Public Works Bureau believes that the construction of Xiangyin Road is particularly important in the city center and will begin building a straight road in the eastern section of Xiangyin Road next month, that is, from Hongbang directly to Jun Gong Road. The original curved road will be designated as a branch road. At the same time, this road will be rebuilt as an asphalt road. The first step in paving asphalt will be temporarily set at four meters.

Municipal Public Works Bureau Changes Street Light On/Off Times 151

To Be Implemented Starting in April

The original street light on time in this city was set from March to August, no later than 6:00 PM, and no later than 5:00 PM in the other months. Later, the Municipal Public Works Bureau, referring to the astronomical observatory's report on sunrise and sunset times, formulated a monthly street light on/off schedule, which was implemented in October of the eighteenth year of the Republic. Now, after further deliberation on actual needs and slight revisions, it is reported that orders have been issued to various electric companies to implement the new schedule uniformly starting in April. Elderly Woman Run Over and Killed by Songhu Train 158

Yesterday at 2:00 PM, an elderly woman, approximately 50 years old, wearing a blue woolen hat and blue cloth clothing, was walking along the Songhu Railway tracks in front of the Parker Milk Company on Jiangwan Road. A small train returning to Shanghai from Songhu was speeding by, and the woman was unable to avoid it, resulting in her entire body being caught under the train. Her brains splattered, and her legs were severed. Her head was completely crushed, a gruesome sight. As of 6:00 PM, no family members had come to claim the body. The railway authorities, due to the lack of family identification, ordered railway workers to temporarily place the woman's body aside, covered with reed mats, to await family members to claim it.

Seventy-Three-Year-Old Woman Falls to Her Death 159

Ni Wangshi, an elderly woman from Suzhou, 73 years old, in good spirits, resided at No. 3 1/2, Maurice Street. Yesterday evening at around 7:00 PM, she hired a carriage to visit a sick child at the Qi family on Fuxu Road. She was warmly welcomed upstairs by the hostess, and they chatted happily. Unexpectedly, misfortune struck. At 8:30 PM, she bid farewell and went downstairs. Inadvertently, she slipped on the stairs and fell, suffering severe head and nose injuries. She died shortly after. Her relatives transported the body to Bao Long Hospital and then to the autopsy center, awaiting notification to the court for examination.

Apprentice Dies, Family Unaware 160

His Mother Has Filed a Complaint

Shen Yinshi, from Haimen, accompanied by witness Shen Guanxing, brought Cao Tangjin to the Second Precinct of the Third District, accusing him of the following: her son, Shen Lincai, 21 years old, was introduced by Shen Guanxing to work as an apprentice in the defendant's rope shop at the age of fifteen. Six years have passed, and he has not yet completed his apprenticeship. In the past, she had taken her son home to stay several times, but Cao, relying on the condition that he had not completed his apprenticeship, did not allow him freedom. The plaintiff was helpless. Now, after six years of apprenticeship and having become an adult, the plaintiff had arranged a marriage for her son in their hometown and needed him to return to meet his bride. Therefore, she rushed to Shanghai, but her son was nowhere to be found. When asked, the defendant claimed that he had gone out to work and would bring him back in about three days. The original intermediary was present at the time. Now, upon going there, she was suddenly told that he had died, which clearly contradicted the previous statement. Her son must have been abused to death, and the body destroyed. She demanded an investigation. When questioned, Cao Tangjin stated that he runs a rope shop in Yangjing and that the apprentice Shen Lincai suffered from dropsy. On December 28th of last year, he was sent to Zhengxin Hospital in Yangshupu for treatment. He died on January 6th of this year. The hospital took the initiative to handle the funeral and buried him in a public cemetery. He had indeed died of illness. Witness Shen Guanxing testified that he runs a car dealership near the defendant's shop. Shen Lincai was the one he introduced to be an apprentice. He did not know if he had died, but the defendant had not notified him. Because Shen Yinshi wanted to ask him for her son, he had no choice but to bring the defendant to the case and request an investigation. The precinct chief, considering that the case involved a life, and a future exhumation would be necessary, immediately transferred it to the local court for thorough investigation.

Three Children Burned to Death on Jiangbei Boat 161

A Jiangbei boat was docked at the East China Sea port in Wusong. Yesterday afternoon at around 1:00 PM, all the men and women on the boat went ashore to shop, leaving only three children to guard the boat. All the children were around ten years old. Subsequently, the three children were playing with fire in the boat, causing a fire to break out on the canvas awning. At that time, the sea breeze was very strong, and the entire boat caught fire in an instant. Residents on the shore noticed and tried to extinguish the fire, only to find that the three children had been burned, their heads and faces charred, their abdomens ruptured, and their intestines spilled out, a gruesome sight. By the time the family members returned from shopping, they had lost their homes and loved ones, and they cried inconsolably by the river.

Female Kidnapper Sentenced to Two Years of Imprisonment 163

Zhang Xiaomao, the three-year-old son of Zhang Qifeng, residing at No. 22 Mill Street in the French Concession, was lured away by the kidnapper Zhang Yushi, in collusion with her lover Zhu Awu, on December 11th of last year. They entrusted the elderly woman Chen Wangshi to sell the child to Zhou Zhangshi in Gaochang Temple. Zhang then took the child to Fujian Province. Detective Liu Youfa of the French police discovered this and apprehended Zhang Yushi, her lover Zhu Awu, and the elderly woman Chen Wangshi. However, the child had already been taken far away to Fujian and could not be brought to court. Yesterday, the police escorted the defendants to the French court for investigation. The plaintiff, Zhang Qifeng, first described the kidnapping, stating that two children had been kidnapped at the time, one eight years old and one three years old. The eight-year-old child cried on the road and was abandoned along the way, and the police department sent him back. The three-year-old child was then sold. He was grateful that they had been apprehended and requested a severe punishment. When questioned, Zhang Yushi confessed that Zhang Laohu, who was at large, had instigated the woman to kidnap the child, and she received 100 yuan for the sale, of which the woman used 30 yuan. Zhu Awu admitted to being in a relationship with Yushi, but the child was kidnapped and sold by Yushi. Although he used 30 yuan from the money afterwards, he did not participate in the kidnapping. His remaining statements were evasive. Chen Wangshi stated that Zhu Awu brought the child to her and entrusted her to sell him to Zhou Zhangshi in Gaochang Temple for 100 yuan. The woman received 10 yuan. When he was brought to her, they falsely claimed that the child's father was dead and that they were unable to raise him, so they were selling him. She did not know he had been kidnapped and asked for leniency. The Chinese and Western judges sentenced Zhang Yushi to two years of imprisonment in a female prison, Zhu Awu to eight months of imprisonment, and Chen Wangshi to four months of imprisonment. The detention period before the verdict was pronounced was allowed to be deducted.

Telegram of Request for Relief from Ba County 167

The Chinese Red Cross Society recently received a telegram from Feng Junyi and others, chairman of the Ba County Temporary Relief Committee, reporting on the severe disaster situation and the establishment of a temporary relief committee. It is hereby disclosed as follows: "Our county is unfortunate, and disasters occur repeatedly. Last year, the weather was unfavorable, with spring floods and summer droughts, resulting in poor harvests and empty granaries. The wealthy have become poor, and the poor have become starving refugees. Throughout the county, there is nothing but devastation. News has spread far and wide, causing widespread grief. The vitality of the people has not yet recovered, and for the past hundred days, there has been no rain, water sources have dried up, and the land is cracked. In addition, our county has a dense population and does not produce much rice. The majority of our food relies on supplies from neighboring counties. In recent months, various places have successively prohibited supplies, resulting in a complete cutoff. Rice prices have soared, costing a hundred or a thousand coins per dou, and there is no market available. As a result, there are cries of distress everywhere, with people waiting to be fed. The phenomenon of refugees fleeing is unprecedented. We believe that the people are the foundation of the nation and food is the people's heaven. Now, it is still far from the new harvest, and the lives of the people in our county are on the verge of collapse. If there is a shortage of food before the new harvest, the tragedy will be even worse. Considering the future, we cannot help but be alarmed. Therefore, on the true date of March, we gathered representatives from various institutions, organizations, and all sectors of the county to establish the Ba County Temporary Relief Committee General Assembly at the county government. We also decided to establish branches and offices in various districts, townships, and towns in the county to actively raise money and materials to relieve the poor. However, our strength is limited, and our knowledge is insufficient. In the face of this difficult task, we are unable to cope. We believe that people from all walks of life are deeply concerned and have a compassion for all people. We hope that you will offer suggestions for disaster relief and generously contribute funds to help the poor so that hundreds of thousands of our suffering compatriots will not be forced to flee and can celebrate a new life. Our gratitude will not be limited to our committee. We are writing this telegram in distress, eager to receive your instructions. Feng Junyi and others of the Ba County Temporary Relief Committee bow."

Seaport Epidemic Prevention Hospital Cracks Down on Illegal Occupation of Land 168

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the Epidemic Prevention Hospital at the North Harbor Mouth on the opposite side of Zhang Huabang in Wusong was established during the late Guangxu period of the Qing Dynasty. It was originally under the jurisdiction of the customs authorities. Later, it was divided into Chinese and foreign sections. The total area of the land is over fifty mu. There was always surplus land outside the hospital, with trees planted around the perimeter and ditches dug as a boundary to isolate it from the local people and prevent the spread of infection. Last year, the National Government sent Wu Liande to take over the jurisdiction of quarantine at seaports throughout the country. The hospital was also simultaneously taken back. Since its establishment, the hospital has occupied a significant position in the country. Unexpectedly, someone paid 57 yuan to the abolished Shangbao Sand Field Bureau and obtained a permit for 9.5 mu of land. When the resident officers and police discovered this, they reported it to Director Wu Liande for handling. Yesterday, Director Wu, accompanied by Secretary Ni Mingshan, and medical officers, went to inspect the site. After observing the terrain, they found that the person who obtained the permit was clearly acting with corrupt motives, intending to encroach on the land and disrupt epidemic prevention. In addition to Secretary Ni consulting the land bureau and the dredging bureau to review the files, they plan to take strict measures to crack down on the illegal occupation.

This association, on behalf of all citizens of the district, asks them to strongly argue with the Public Works Department and insist to the end to achieve the goal of cancellation, which will benefit the citizens. This letter was sent out yesterday.

Seamen's Union Assists Workers Affected by Yangtze River Ship Disaster 171

The Seamen's Union sent a telegram to the Central Government, stating: "To the Nanjing Central Training Department, National Government, Ministry of Industry, Ministry of Transportation, and Ministry of Foreign Affairs: We have received a report from Ling Hong and others, workers affected by the Yangtze River ship disaster of the French Lacheng Company, stating that at 2:05 PM on the 16th of this month, the ship encountered dense fog near the Beiyu Mountain Lighthouse in Zhejiang Province and struck a reef, causing the ship's bow to rupture. The captain sounded the bell and ordered the engine room to reverse the engines. Within just twenty minutes, the ship sank. Previously, Ling Hong, the second comprador, twice personally asked the captain to send a radio distress call, but he refused to do so and did not allow anyone to escape. As a result, the victims had no choice but to jump into the water and escape, in a state of extreme panic. It is estimated that eleven crew members, two female passengers and maids from the grand dining room, and one female passenger from the second class cabin drowned. All their belongings were lost. The captain of the ship was rescued by staff members and taken to the nearby mountainside, where they gathered grass and wood to light a fire to keep warm. At midnight on the 17th, a merchant ship passed by, and they asked the lighthouse to send a telegram. On the morning of the 18th, they saw the French warship Mali arrive to rescue them. On the morning of the 19th, they returned to Shanghai by warship and demanded that the Lacheng Company compensate them for their losses in advance, but the company only agreed to give each person 15 yuan. There are currently over fifty crew members staying at the French police station on Feifei Road, which is temporarily providing food. The company uses the Haifang General Office as an excuse and refuses to take any action or provide any assistance. Please provide strong assistance. According to the report, the captain did not send a telegram or reverse the engines, causing the ship to sink and many lives to be lost. According to the law, he deserves punishment. The losses of the surviving workers are enormous, and the deceased are冤沉 under the sea. The company's improper employment makes it fully responsible for compensation and condolences. However, after our association sent personnel to negotiate, the company ignored it. We are therefore sending this telegram to your departments, requesting that you forward it to the Shanghai Municipal Government for assistance in handling the matter to save the affected workers. We await your instructions. The Chinese Seamen's Industrial Federation Organizing Committee, seal."

Prohibition of Superstitious Acts During Qingming Festival 173

Proclamation by the Shanghai County Government

The Shanghai County Government issued a proclamation yesterday, stating: "Regarding the matter of a proclamation, according to the proposal of the Fifth District Chief at the Twelfth District Chief Meeting, during the Qingming Festival, villagers arbitrarily burn paper money and alcohol, engaging in superstitious activities, and requesting that a proclamation be issued to prohibit this in order to conserve people's wealth. After discussion, it was decided to investigate the matter. As this matter was previously proclaimed and ordered by the County Public Security Bureau and the District Chiefs to investigate and advise against it last year, we hereby issue a proclamation to all the people of the county, in addition to ordering the County Public Security Bureau and the District Chiefs, to make them fully aware that burning paper money is a superstitious custom, and if relatives visit each other, feasting with alcohol is even more meaningless. All must comply, mutually advise, and abolish these practices. It is imperative. This proclamation is hereby issued."

Young Monk Attempts Suicide by Drowning, Rescued 174

Zhang Shunhua, His Life Was Not Destined to End

Shunhua, a boy of fifteen, is from Ningbo. When he was five years old, his biological mother, due to poverty and difficult living conditions, had no choice but to sell Shunhua to a monk with the Dharma name Shichun as a disciple. He currently resides at No. 1 Gongqing Lane, Tangjia Lane, Tianbao Road, Zhabei. Shunhua is naturally dull, so he cannot remember the scriptures that Shichun teaches him to recite. Therefore, he does not please his master and is often whipped. Shunhua could not bear the hardship. The previous evening, the monk Shichun again ordered him to recite the scriptures, but he could not fulfill the request. As a result, he was once again punished and suffered greatly. Shunhua, overwhelmed with sadness, had the thought of committing suicide. Taking advantage of his master's unpreparedness, he secretly slipped out and went to the Youche Wharf, Puhui, in the South City, and jumped into the river. Before long, he surfaced. At that time, a coal boat was passing by. The boat owner, Mr. Hou, glimpsed a boy floating on the river and immediately went forward to rescue him. After rescuing Shunhua, he helped him to the side of the boat, warmed his body, and then used artificial respiration to revive him. After questioning him about the situation, he could not help but feel compassion for him. He quickly changed Shunhua's wet clothes and then let him stay overnight. Yesterday morning at about 8:00 AM, he reported the matter to Yin Wanyou, the guard of the Eighteenth Precinct, who took him to the relevant precinct of the First District. The precinct chief took the case and, after a preliminary interrogation, ordered him to prepare a document and send it to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for placement.

The Treatment Method for Sensing External Pathogens 176

Mr. Qin Bowei, a Chinese medicine doctor from Shangwen Road, Xiaoximen, this city, after publishing an article on the prediction of seasonal epidemics on the 5th of this month, indeed, almost no family could escape the prevalent influenza with symptoms of chills, fever, and cough. Mr. Qin told people yesterday that the seasonal epidemic is still rampant, but it is different from before. Many patients have blood in their sputum, or cough up blood from their entire mouth, or bleed from their nose, with very high fever, headache, and chest pain. Therefore, the previous method of dispelling and relieving is no longer effective, and the method of clearing and relieving must be used. With proper treatment, although there is no danger, the time is longer. If treatment is delayed or excessive sweating is induced, it can easily lead to mental confusion and irritability, so attention must be paid. Furthermore, Mr. Qin's younger brother, Dr. Qin Youan, who has studied medicine with his brother, has been practicing medicine since last year. Recently, he believes that the changeable weather this spring easily causes people to be susceptible to external pathogens, leading to prolonged illness. When patients first feel headache, nasal congestion, and aversion to cold, it indicates that the cold pathogen has just entered, being at the Taiyang meridian. The Inner Classic says, "If it is in the skin, it can be released by sweating." Based on research findings, he learned from this principle and modified the method of diaphoresis, using a simple steam wash treatment, which is extremely convenient. The prescription is two liang of Perilla leaves, four qian of Mentha (added later), eight qian of Schizonepeta, and eight qian of Saposhnikovia. Place the above four herbs in a pot, add a large amount of water, boil for a few boils, and then pour it into a washbasin. Have the patient lower their head over the basin, making sure it is directly above the basin, and cover it with a wrapper or a sheet, allowing the hot steam to rise without leakage. The mouth must be kept open to allow saliva to flow out until a slight sweat is felt on the back. After that, avoid wind at all costs. Mild cases need only one treatment, severe cases no more than two, and all are effective. This is specially recorded to inform the citizens, as a truly simple and convenient method for prevention and treatment.

The Registration of Zhenghua Silver Company is Still Difficult to Approve 181

The Ministry of Finance previously received an application from the Zhenghua Silver Company in this city for registration. Because the company's capital was only 50,000 yuan, which was insufficient to fund operations, it was disapproved. Subsequently, the company sent a letter through the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, stating that the current laws and regulations did not have a minimum limit for the qualifications of silver companies, and detailed the reasons, requesting approval for prior registration. Now, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce received another reply from the Ministry of Finance yesterday, stating: "Received the presentation. Shanghai is a prosperous commercial area. The silver company mainly engages in straw hat export financing, and a capital of 50,000 yuan is insufficient for its operations. Although the current laws and regulations do not have a minimum limit, the Ministry should still consider the circumstances, weigh the pros and cons, and prevent the occurrence of risks. The request for registration is difficult to approve." The Chamber has forwarded this reply to the Zhenghua Silver Company for review.

Free Talk

A Word of Wisdom 185

— Qiushui

▲ Seeking forgiveness is the beggar's hiding place. We should repay our debts.

▲ Long dresses seem to make modern girls reveal their solemnity slightly. Unfortunately, however, long dresses have the same purpose as advertisements.

▲ A person cannot make progress in his career if he has no enemies. Because enemies can frankly point out your shortcomings, like an ideal good friend.

▲ Love smiles at brave people, sneers at cowardly husbands, and laughs loudly at madmen.

▲ Although the speed of a car is faster than that of a carriage, when a pair of modern rural girls travel in the suburbs by car, occasionally, they cannot help themselves, and the car is not as safe as a carriage.

▲ Men can be too old to dance, to work, or to play games. However, when he sees a beautiful girl, he can't help but tidy up his clothes and make a vigorous effort.

▲ A man's love cannot gain more knowledge through experience. It is common to see them fail in this love and repeat the same mistakes the second time.

▲ There are many women who don't know how to choose a husband in their lives. It is too late to regret when they are old and approaching death.

▲ Newly married men and women are like two newly acquainted children. They cannot become acquainted until after a fight.

▲ Marriage is like national politics. There are always people who support it, oppose it, or even stir up trouble from it.

Heartfelt Words from Huanglu 186

— Zheng Yimei

It has not been ten days since Fanshan passed away, and now we hear that Yuan Hanyun has also left us. I am overwhelmed with grief for the loss of old friends. My brother-in-law, Zhou Wuzhu, had a cordial relationship with Hanyun as host and guest. I also made friends through literature and often exchanged letters. I know a thing or two about his life. Hanyun, whose taboo name was Kewen, was the second child. His courtesy name was Baocun, also written as Baocen. His pseudonym was Guian. He once obtained Zhao Feiyan's jade ring, considering it a rare stroke of luck from the remnants of the palace's powder and rouge. He engraved a seal with the inscription "Yan Huan" to commemorate his treasure, using it in his poems and writings. He possessed the talent of both a poet and a military advisor. Among the Seven Talents of Xuan Nan, Hanyun was the leader. He once had a collection of poems printed in vermilion ink, corrected by Yi Shifu. Unfortunately, it was not widely circulated, and now it is out of print with no copies remaining. His occasional short couplets and phrases were filled with the magic of flying flowers and dancing butterflies between the lines. Actors and actresses, as well as people from the pleasure district, often obtained his couplets. Hanyun was known for his romanticism and fondness for entertainment. Hanyun was also able to perform on stage. He was particularly good at "Examining the Head and Stabbing Tang." In the past, when he lived in Shanghai, he was often invited to perform in dramas to raise funds for local public welfare. Hanyun never declined and often captivated the audience with his beautiful songs. He had a habit of enjoying the scenery, always had a couch set up, and treated night as day. He would wear short clothes and go barefoot. Even when guests arrived, he was not constrained. He would lie on the couch and browse through books. When he read something he liked, he would immediately grab a pen and write comments. He could lie on his back and write small characters on the margins of the book with his head. His handwriting was elegant and neat, surpassing that of previous calligraphers. People from all over the country sought his calligraphy, wearing down his doorstep. He occasionally painted, depicting flowers and plants with a few strokes, and they were filled with fragrance and ease. The interest was in the meaning, not in the standard. Truly, only a clever person could do it. He was lazy and disdainful of official hats and robes. A certain important person admired his talent and invited him to Zhejiang, specially building a fine residence by the Ming Sheng Lake for him to live in. Hanyun said that the beauty of the lake and mountains should not be wasted. He asked for a month to enjoy the scenery. After that, he would serve and work hard. The important person did not force him. Unexpectedly, after a few weeks, he secretly returned to his Shanghai residence. When the important person came to urge him in person, he only felt a sense of loss. His unruliness was like this. His appearance was slightly similar to that of General Haiming. A certain newspaper published the photos of the two together. Hanyun was in military uniform, and Haiming was in Confucian clothing. It was even more difficult to distinguish who was a tiger and who was a scholar. It was a beautiful story at the time. He had a sharp eye for appreciating antiques. However, he had strong self-confidence. Occasionally, he would buy fake goods. Even if someone told him the truth, he would not listen. He thought it was nonsense. When told again, he would scold, saying, "If I can get two of such fake goods, I would be willing to pay a heavy price to get them." He also liked to caress ancient coins. The year before last, he used an ancient coin as a betrothal gift for his son Bochong's engagement. His father-in-law, Fang Dishan, was also a famous scholar, so he could deeply sympathize with his unconventional customs. His thriftiness was a model for the world. His published works include "Huan Shang Private Records" and "Hanyun's Essays." It is said that Hanyun wrote a diary every day, without interruption in summer or winter, for nearly twenty years. It contains many secrets of the court and anecdotes of poetry and wine. If it is engraved, it will be an immortal work.

Juan'an Hanyun was one of my dearest friends in my life. When I was a guest in Shanghai in the past, we met almost every day. Poems and articles were exchanged, accumulating into a volume over time. He helped me a lot when I edited magazines such as "Half-Month Violet." In recent years, I have been living in Tianjin, and news has been scarce. I originally planned to go north to visit him in the late spring of this year. Unexpectedly, the bad news came and he rushed to Yulou Terrace. Looking back on the past, I am extremely sad. My brother has a wealth of writings. I have personally seen his diaries before. Every word is carefully written, and the articles are both practical and beautiful. Compared to Li Yuke's diary, it is not much different. I secretly hope that all my friends in the country will do their best to collect his posthumous works and compile them into a volume to be engraved and passed down for a long time.

Random Talks in the Art Garden 187

— Chen Boying

Wu Changshuo (缶老) was initially known for his seal carving by Wu Dacheng and Yang Xian. His name gradually became known in Jiangzuo. When he was strong, he listened to the drum in Suzhou. He was unruly and somewhat arrogant. The superiors did not like him very much. Zhang Zuyi from Tongcheng was friendly with him. Zhang was good at official script, and Wu was good at seal script. Both had a passion for bronze and stone inscriptions. Zhang was also good at seal carving, with a charming touch in his vigorous style. Each established their own style. Both gentlemen were fat, short, and beardless. Viewers sometimes mistakenly thought they were eunuchs. Therefore, Wu called himself the Beardless Old Man in his later years. Wu's seals are better than others because they are round and tight. When others are arrogant, they only resemble his reclining posture. He uses a large knife to carve stones. My friend Zhang Tianzhou jokingly called him "Wu Junqing, the Wu Seal Star with the Big Knife." Tianzhou also loved to use a big knife for seal carving. When he was in a hurry, he did not choose his tools. He could make words with nail heads and scissor ends. It was similar to the copper seals of the Xin Mang Dynasty. He painted landscapes in a heavy and ancient style. There was no equal at the time. Wu was not good at painting, but his pine and bamboo paintings were quite interesting when they were executed with seal script. When he used red, it was thick and without measure. When people saw it, they said, "Let him see some colors." It could evoke a sigh.

A Brief Talk on Rainbow Garments and Feathered Robes 188

— Wu Jiren

The Star Opera Society has been established for more than a year. I am sincerely stingy and have not been able to participate in the rehearsals and listen to the elegant music. I am deeply regretful. On the 22nd of this month, the company held a concert at Dumei Road. The company's colleagues all appeared on stage, and it is impossible not to record it. Unfortunately, I am completely ignorant of Peking Opera. I only feel that the clear singing is graceful and pleasing to the eye and ear. Helpless, I can only pick up the saliva of the old man next door who spoke about the art of drama and use it for the entertainment of my fellow writers.

▲ Zhang Shichuan's Two Major Plays: The famous director Mr. Zhang Shichuan usually studies the art of the screen and has never performed in person. Since the new film "The Scandalous History of the Screen" came out, Mr. Zhang's face has appeared on the screen for the first time. Since the success of "The Singing Girl Red Peony," he once showed his face on the red carpet. He actually had two major plays. On that day, he played Huang Tianba in "Falling Horse Lake," and his voice was clear and could compete with the famous amateur opera singer Detian Resident. In "The Three Courts Joint Trial," he played the Red Robe Commissioner with subtle expressions and without any hesitation. It was not easy.

▲ Zhou Jianyun's Steady Singing and Acting: Mr. Zhou Jianyun, the president of the opera company, also sang two good plays. He and Ms. Ying Yunwen performed "Visiting Mother," and he and Ms. Huang Xuexuan performed "Nantianmen." Mr. Zhou has been a ticket holder for a long time, and his acting is skilled, and his stage steps are steady. He does not lose the model of his predecessors. The lines are not sloppy. It is a pity that his voice has lost its luster. I think Mr. Zhou is too hard and has little rest.

▲ Wang Xuan and Jing Lin's Performance of Lotus Lantern: Mr. Wang Yushu and Ms. Xuan Jinglin performed "Lotus Lantern" together on the same day, which can be called evenly matched. They have already entered the realm of magic. Mr. Wang is a famous senior in the ticket circle and can perform many plays. Occasionally, he can completely get rid of the mundane atmosphere when he appears on stage. Ms. Xuan's singing voice is gentle and pleasant, and she has deeply mastered the essence of Yu Shuang. In addition, her facial expressions and gestures are all dramatic. It is no wonder that she is the mainstay of the Star Opera Company. Only Xuan can do it.

▲ The Hard Work of the Martial Arts Play: The most dedicated martial arts plays were "Baishuitan," performed by Xu Xinfu and Wu Wanxiang, and "Jiamengguan," performed by Huang Tianyin and Wu Wanxiang. Wanxiang is proficient in martial arts, and Xinfu is a director of martial arts films. He has the demeanor of a Confucian scholar and actually reversed his original appearance. Dong Tianya has been performing amateur opera for a long time, and his skills are proficient and do not lose their rules. All three gentlemen have recently been studying with Mr. Chen Yuelou. Their deep understanding of martial arts is well-founded.

▲ Red Peony's Yutangchun: The most flavorful night play was "Little Cowherd," performed by Zheng Xiaoqiu and Gu Meijun. This play depicts the love of young children, and it is beautiful without being obscene. It is rare. The finale was "The Three Courts Joint Trial," performed by Hu Die, the protagonist of Red Peony, and Mr. Wang Xianzai and other members. Hu Die won with her expressions, and Xianzai won with his lines. The old man continued, "My old eyes are dim and I cannot give an accurate evaluation. However, such achievements are already rare. In addition, all the artists are talented. If they can work harder, the next time will be even more spectacular."

Zhao Tieqiao After Death 189

— Manyin

Zhao Tieqiao was also a famous scholar from Sichuan. He has a considerable history of contributions to the revolution. Two years ago, he had a relationship with the famous prostitute Xue Lin in the Qinhuai River area, which was well known. However, he did not lose his elegance as a celebrity. Later, he became a commissioner of the Shanghai China Merchants Bureau, but he was assassinated. After his death, he was extremely desolate. It is said that although Zhao was a commissioner of the China Merchants Bureau, at this time, the bureau was in a state of turmoil. The Northern Expedition was in full swing, and he was busy dispatching ships, transporting soldiers and weapons. People regarded him as a fat cat, but he was not greedy. He was killed in middle age, leaving behind many children, all of whom were young. (It was seen in a certain newspaper that Zhao Guangzu was mentioned, with a note stating that he was Zhao Tieqiao's son. In fact, there is another Zhao Guangzu in Shanghai.) Later, when the government discussed Zhao's pension, in addition to a special grant of 1,000 yuan for funeral expenses, the Ministry of Personnel assessed and approved a pension of 720 yuan per year for his family, based on one-tenth of his last monthly salary of 600 yuan, in accordance with the regulations on pensions for officials. In addition, in accordance with the same regulations, a one-time pension of 1,200 yuan, equivalent to two months' salary, was granted to the family. However, the Ministry of Personnel's report stated that the deceased commissioner had devoted himself to the revolution for more than 20 years, reorganized the shipping business, and facilitated military operations. His achievements were great, and his previous merits should be commemorated. This assessment was based on regulations and was not a reward for revolutionary achievements. Later, after the State Council meeting, a special one-time pension of 3,000 yuan and an annual pension of 960 yuan were granted to the family of the late Commissioner Zhao. This was very generous, even in the National Government. However, with this monthly pension of 80 yuan, Mrs. Zhao had to raise her many children, which was very hard. I remember in the autumn of last year, Zhao Tieqiao's daughter, Zhao Yinmei, who was only 12 or 13 years old, was studying at a certain girls' school. There was a teacher who did not know that Miss Zhao was Tieqiao's daughter. Once, in class, when discussing Chinese shipping, he criticized Zhao Tieqiao's management of the China Merchants Bureau, saying that it had no achievements. Although Miss Zhao was young, she remembered that her father had been brutally murdered, and after his death, someone was still criticizing her father in front of her. She immediately stood up and left the classroom, crying bitterly. After returning home, the mother and daughter hugged each other and cried. Since then, she never went back to that school. Alas, is this not a true fact that must bring tears?

Indian Travels (6) 190

— Linghua

Regarding the caste system, the doctor said that this system still exists today, but it is slightly more flexible. The first class is the Brahmin caste. All monks must come from this caste. Other castes are not allowed. The second is the Kshatriya caste, the warrior class. The third is the merchant class. The fourth is the Sudra caste, the servant class. The four castes are not allowed to intermarry. The son of a farmer is always a farmer, and the son of a worker is always a worker, as Guanzi of China said. Buddha wanted to break this system, but in the end, people did not believe in his teachings. It can also be seen how great its power is. From this, we can know the importance of Indian monks. It has a long history. Because only the first class can become monks. Other classes are not allowed. Things are rare and strange. They are originally nobles, and becoming monks is even more noble. However, since the entry of the British into India, the Indian people felt the pressure of foreign forces, and the movement for liberation began. Recently, new ideas have emerged, and there have been gradual changes.

At 2 pm this afternoon, the Social Education Association gave a lecture. There were Tan Jueshi, Lai Wei, Zhang Guoji, and others. Consul Lu and his wife were also in attendance and took photos. At 5 pm, a general meeting was held at the Indian Mahayana Buddhist Association Lecture Hall. The principal of the girls' school, Sarala Dervi, presided over the meeting. She is the niece of Tagore. At that time, six or seven hundred people attended the meeting. Ms. West was also there. Consul Lu Chunfang and his wife were also there. Everyone asked Lu to give a speech. After my speech, the chairman translated it into Bengali. There was also an old philosopher, Krishna, who was 70 years old and had been running a newspaper for 50 years. He gave a loud speech about the great light of Eastern culture, saying that all beings could be saved from now on. The audience was moved. Then his daughter, Mrs. Boss, sang praises. The meeting adjourned at 7 pm.

On the 24th, I visited Master Daojie but did not meet him. I met a Burmese student at 8 Eden Hospital road. This is the Burmese Monks' Buddhist Temple. All Burmese monks and students who worship Buddha can live here. Food is self-provided. It costs more than ten yuan per month. Chinese people can also live there. When I asked how many Burmese students there were, they replied more than ten. The temple cost more than 50,000 yuan and is used to entertain Burmese people. Now, there are Burmese Monks' Buddhist Temples in all the Buddhist sites. Chinese people can all live there. Food is self-provided. Then, Burmese Buddhists are worthy of being Buddhist heroes. The Burmese are humble, easy-going and approachable, like calm water without waves. The Indians have a vast and boundless aura, and their bodies are also tall, very different from the Burmese. The Burmese should naturally belong to India, but now they are said to be separate and independent. This is due to the British political movement.

At 5 pm on the 25th, Mrs. Sen invited me to a tea party. Lu and his wife were both there. The Sen family lived in London for 17 years and have now returned. They know many English gentlemen and ladies, such as Russell Wells and others. They also like Chinese people very much. Chinese art is the best in the world. Japanese art is also famous, but not as good. She told me to wait a few weeks, and Tagore will return to China. We can discuss the method of the world cultural movement together. I saw a Western store sign in the market that said China & glass, which is porcelain and glass. They use the word "支那", from which we know that porcelain is called China.

Powerful Fluctuations in Finance and Gold Markets 191

Terrible Ups and Downs: Yesterday, March 26th, the gold price experienced dramatic changes, soaring and then plummeting, fluctuating wildly by six or seven taels in an instant. Giant waves and angry tides were seen again in the market. From morning till night, there were a total of sixteen taels of twists and turns, ultimately ending with a slight drop. People were alarmed, and the chaotic scene was indescribable. Although foreign exchange rates strengthened and then weakened, the change was not as drastic as in the gold market. Quoted prices were reduced by one level. Some dealers were first caught short and then covered their positions. Transactions on the surface were varied. In the morning session, Yuan Mao Yong, Da De Cheng, and Wu Pin, among others, were buying, while Heng Xing and Yong Heng, among others, were selling heavily. Overseas silver markets also reported declines, so the gold price suddenly reached a peak, even breaking through the 700 tael mark. Later, merchants from Guangdong and other places were inclined to sell, leading to a sharp downward turn, with a plunge of ten taels. However, the situation was confusing. It was rumored that Siam was selling a large quantity of silver ingots, so there was a slight rise. At noon, selling pressure intensified again, and the market softened again. In the afternoon session, Yong Heng, Yu Da, and others continued to sell, especially as the shortage of drafts worsened, suddenly falling below 690 taels.

A Rapid Opening: The May opening in the morning surged by ten taels and four qian to 699 taels. Large bars fell by 5/16, and the silver price fell by 3/4. The European market was calm, and private telegrams also fell by 5/8. Wu Pin, Yuan Mao Yong, Zhi Feng Yong, and others competed to buy, driving the price from 98 taels to 702 taels and five qian. Drafts settled in British gold were not slack. Mai Hang quoted 8125 for forward contracts. Soon, Heng Xing and Yong Heng both sold, and British gold could be settled at 875, causing the price to fall to 96 taels. When the first exchange rate was announced, it was reduced by 25, with US dollars at 50 cents and Japanese yen at 2.75 fen, making it 98 taels. But in a moment, it depreciated by more than three taels, reaching 94 taels and five qian. Wu Pin and others sold, and Fu Chang and others bought, partly because British and Japanese banks were absorbing currency. Forward British gold was at 9375, so the price rose to 700 taels and five qian. Later, Heng Xing, Da De Cheng, and others continued to sell, and in an instant, the price fell by as much as seven or eight taels. Around 10 o'clock, it was 92 taels and five qian. Suddenly, it was heard that a large quantity of silver had been sold abroad. People's spirits lifted, and Yuan Mao Yong, Wu Pin, Fu Yu, and others all came to buy. Banks also traded July British gold at 875, and Hua Bi offered recent British gold at 8125, leading to a surge of more than eight taels, reaching 701 taels at 10:15. Later, Yong Heng and others continued to sell, and Wu Pin's hedging positions also came to sell, and with British gold weakening, the price plunged by six or seven taels, reaching 94 taels and a half after 10:30. Banks then absorbed June British gold at 875, reaching 700 taels at 11:15. Afterwards, the price fluctuated erratically, with different exchanges showing divergent trends. There were about three or four taels of price differences. After 11:45, the market became increasingly fatigued. Sellers were strong on the surface. At noon, the price was 91 taels and five qian, and at the closing, it was 93 taels, with a further fluctuation of more than one tael, rising again to 94 taels. Initially, it was supported, but soon it could not hold, depreciating by three or four taels, with only two or three taels of rebound. After 2:45, it felt particularly weak. However, the differences in entry and exit among exchanges varied. Heng Xing then bought, adding three taels, reaching 89 taels and a half. However, selling pressure did not cease. By the 4:30 closing, the price was only 86 taels and five qian. At this time, Wan Xing and Shun Li came to buy, suddenly pulling the price up by three or four taels, reaching slightly above 90 taels, a decrease of two taels and one qian compared to the previous day (according to the listed price). If calculated according to the black market, it was still up by two taels. Straight tribute woolen cloth has also suddenly turned to an upward trend, likely due to the gradual scarcity of existing stock. Moganshan Hunting Goose is heavily discounted at 3 qian 5 fen. Yuan Yang yarn is also holding firm; Dian Qiuxiang is steadily rising, selling for 10 liang 6 qian, Yuan Ji Beauty 10 liang 3 qian, and Small Beauty remains at 12 liang 5 qian. Among all the goods, only fine serge still lacks a good outlook, mainly due to the abundance of inventory. Customer groups are primarily from the Yangtze River and Jiangxi regions, with groups from Hankou and Qingdao also showing more activity than before. The overall trend for Western goods is stable; plain pongee is seeing some transactions on this street, with Zhonghe goods at 7 qian and Lulin goods at 7 qian 2 fen 5 li, it is said.

Silk and Tea: Pierced Cocoon Sales Brisk, Prices Firm 205

Last year's production of pierced cocoons in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces was not strong, while demand from domestic silk factories is high, resulting in supply falling short of demand. The market is becoming increasingly firm. The existing stock in Shanghai is limited. Yesterday, a merchant from the mainland brought 35 dan of Hangzhou pierced cocoons, priced at 62 liang.

Metals: Black Iron Sheet Drops Another 2 Qian 5 Fen 206

Recently, due to oversupply, the market for 18-gauge black iron sheets has been unusually weak. Even traditionally well-selling factories have seen limited actual use recently, so they lack purchases. Therefore, the sluggishness of the market is rare among all metal goods. The price is only 11 liang 7 qian 5 fen, down another 2 qian 5 fen from before. Spot transactions in the market are also few and far between, it is said.

White Iron Sheet Waits for its Opportunity 207

The market for 24-gauge and 26-gauge white iron sheets has been quiet for a long time, so standards have also become sluggish. In the past three or four days, construction groups have inquired, and railway and military factories have also reportedly made purchases. Therefore, market negotiations have suddenly become lively, morale is strong, and standards are rebounding. It is estimated that 24-gauge sells for 15 liang 5 qian per dan, and 26-gauge for 17 liang, which is 2 qian 5 fen higher than the previous market price. It is said that over 400 dan were sold yesterday, it is said.

New Iron Wire Expected to Arrive 208

New iron wire has been out of stock for a long time, causing general purchasers to yearn for it like a prolonged drought hoping for a rain dragon. Recently, according to news from foreign firms, it is said that 400 to 500 barrels of this commodity will be in stock before the 10th of next month. Therefore, the market prospects are bound to be lively, it is said.

600 boxes of tea loaded for France today.

160 pieces of egg yolk and egg white shipped to France today.

460 pieces of white rattan loaded from Southeast Asia.

Manuscript Guidelines for the Arts Section 209

(1) Articles should be related to the latest news, reviews, and introductions of domestic and international art (painting, music, sculpture, architecture, drama, etc.) and women's studies.

(2) Photographs should be limited to recent portraits of domestic and international artists and their works, as well as various relevant photographs.

(4) The number of words in each article should not exceed 2,000.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

Manuscripts should be written horizontally, neatly, and legibly. Western text should be minimized. If it is necessary to quote original text, it must be attached below the translated text.

(7) Do not use blue ink for illustrations in the manuscript, and do not use colored paper. White paper and black ink must be used.

(8) Please indicate on the manuscript that it is for the Arts Section Editorial Department.

(9) Whether the manuscript is published or not, it will generally not be returned. If it must be returned, it should be stated in advance and sufficient postage should be attached.

(10) Remuneration for articles is divided into three types: four yuan, three yuan, and two yuan per thousand words. The same applies to illustrations and photographs per piece. Remuneration for special manuscripts will be calculated separately.

Manuscript Guidelines for Book and Newspaper Introductions 210

(1) Articles should be limited to introductions of new domestic and international publications. In addition to literary works, all political, economic, legal, scientific, educational...and pictorials are included in the introductions. However, trivial books and newspapers will not be introduced.

(2) Illustrations should be limited to recent works by new domestic and international artists and illustrations related to the text.

(3) Articles on textual research or research on ancient Chinese books will not be published.

(4) Illustrations and photographs should be limited to those related to the text.

(5) The number of words in each article should not exceed 3,000.

(6) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(7) Do not use blue ink for illustrations, and do not use colored paper. White paper and black ink must be used.

(8) Please indicate on the manuscript that it is for the Book and Newspaper Introduction Editorial Department.

(9) Whether the manuscript is published or not, will not be returned. If it must be returned, it should be stated in advance and sufficient postage should be attached.

(10) Remuneration for articles is divided into three types: three yuan, two yuan, and one yuan per thousand words. The same applies to illustrations and photographs. Remuneration for special manuscripts will be calculated separately.

(10) Remuneration for articles is divided into three types: three yuan, two yuan, and one yuan per thousand words. The same applies to illustrations and photographs per piece. Remuneration for special manuscripts will be calculated separately.

Youth Corner

Deadline Extension for Essay Contest of The Era Youth Society 211

— Wen

The Era Youth Society was originally a product of adapting to the environment. We can clearly see its past performance in its work. In recent years, the division and morbidity within the youth community have indeed created a widespread crisis of misfortune. On the one hand, due to the fundamental deformity of China's education system and the survival of feudal remnants in inland society, as well as the harassment of warlords and communist bandits, the threat of the pain of being out of school frequently strikes the hearts of young people. At the same time, the coercion of imperialism with weapons to invade has caused the original general economic organization of Chinese society to undergo a shaking reflection. As a result, the severity of intellectual unemployment has added another layer of sorrow. Thus, young people, in addition to being out of school, have suffered the misfortune of increased unemployment. The development of these two major problems has indeed led young people to a path of extreme depression. Therefore, some young people, seeing that the trend of the times cannot be constantly stifled, have risen up to make a call. We can generally see this point in the arguments published in their "Era Youth." Recently, they have been even more focused on their work. In order to meet the general desires, they have specifically expanded the original space several times, with both quality and quantity advancing simultaneously. It is truly commendable that so many students can achieve such results. Regarding the essay contest, I have previously introduced it in an article. Recently, I heard that the society, in order to seek a more comprehensive consideration, has specifically extended the deadline to April 20. Because its topics, "Several Important Issues for Young People of the Era" and "Literature and Politics," are precisely of great connection to the current era and young people themselves, it is natural to need more excellent works in order to inspect the degree of awakening of the general youth. There have also been submissions from inland areas such as Hangzhou, which shows the potential of its promotion. In order to increase interest, the society has also prepared cash prizes: thirty yuan for the first place, twenty yuan for the second place, ten yuan for the third place, and commemorative gifts for the fourth to tenth places. In addition to being published in "Era Youth," the selected manuscripts are also intended to be compiled into a special collection, with the author's photograph attached to the front of the volume for visual clarity. It is hoped that young people standing on the stage of the era will actively respond to the call, so that we can express the irrepressible emotions in our hearts.

Datong University Student Self-Government Association 212

— Dong

Holds Representative Assembly

Since its establishment, Datong University has had a close-knit and sound student association, which has existed for seven years. The school is progressing rapidly, and the number of students increases every year, now exceeding 1,600. The achievements of the student association are also progressing along with it. Since the beginning of this spring semester, the previous student association has followed the central government's regulations on the organizational outline of student self-government associations, and has actively prepared for re-election. Each college and department elected one representative out of every twenty people. The all-school representative assembly was held yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM in classroom 212. More than sixty people attended, including Xie Shoufu, Xie Zhimin, Tong Shiquan, and Ms. Hu Kewen, Chen Jing, etc. The atmosphere at the meeting was quite enthusiastic. The officers of the assembly were the presidium Xu Zexiang, Wu Daquan, and Secretary Dai Daxin. First, Chairman Xu Zexiang gave the opening remarks, outlining four points: (1) The past history and spirit of the student association; (2) The reasons and process for changing from a student association to a self-government association; (3) The meaning of self-government; (4) The hope that today's assembly will review the work of the past student association, set the direction for future work, and elect leaders to lead the work of the self-government association to achieve the meaning of self-government and the mission it bears. Next, President Ou Yuanhuai gave a speech, encouraging and rewarding, hoping that all key members would work together in harmony, implement the spirit of cooperation, and assist in the development of school affairs. Next, Director of Group Education Yu Zhihan gave a speech, and the representative of the district branch Cui Buwu gave a speech. The discussion items should have been carried out, but later, due to the large number of important proposals received by the secretariat from each college and department, and due to time constraints, the assembly decided to leave them for the next discussion. The agenda was immediately changed to hold elections. As a result, Wang Jianmin, Xu Zexiang, and Zhou Zhaoshao were elected as the presidium of the representative assembly, and Wang Ruinian, Cui Buwu, Cheng Liangneng, and fifteen others were elected as members of the executive committee. The meeting adjourned at 4:00 PM.

"Duckweed Shadows" of the Duckweed Shadow Society 213

— Wen

We must also say that the youth's keen love for literature and art is a good phenomenon. Since the May Fourth New Culture Movement, the youth's inclination to refined life has shifted into a new stage. Their pursuit of literature and art has the intention of making up for shortcomings and comforting the soul. Although it is inevitable that many are reflections of the self, it is not necessarily a sign of young people's urgent search for a spiritual home in a certain sense. In such a bad environment, all realities cannot satisfy desires, so it is natural to pour into this aspect. Therefore, such a rising trend is not an accidental fact. In recent years, the organization of youth literary groups has been increasing day by day, as we can see from the various schools. Not long ago, we discovered another literary collective organized by young people from various schools, called the Duckweed Shadow Society. The leaders are Zhang Yifei, Mei Yonggeng, Mei Hongying, etc. They published a half-open newspaper called "Duckweed Shadows" monthly, which has now been published to the third issue. In the "Inaugural Remarks," they explained their attitude in this way:

The Duckweed Shadow Society is organized by several sincere young people. Hot blood is on our bodies, and pens are in our hands. This small newspaper is to reveal our sincere emotions. The era is so damn worthy. Young people in this era, as long as your soul has not been lost and your senses have not become numb, who does not feel a kind of youthful sorrow? Several of us sincere young people cannot stand the ugliness of society and cannot bear the depression in our hearts. Therefore, we are damned by everything. We express the real emotions in our hearts. Therefore, we disregarded everything and created this small garden.

From this point of view, their self-composition in the exploration of literature and art is very strong. However, from another perspective, it is precisely a manifestation of the lack of consciousness among the general youth. They often like to act recklessly as a cultivation act, which is of course very regrettable. I have not been able to clearly understand the meaning of "Duckweed Shadows" in its naming, but judging from the content of the three issues that have been published, it is just like the floating shadows of duckweed in life, and the outpouring of a kind of sentimentality is indeed extremely strong. Although we cannot deny the inherent real demands of this kind of lament, we, as young people standing on such a stage of the times, do not need to pick up a pen to write some curse words, and think that we are mentally happy. I should have greater aspirations and also a plan to enrich our lives. Most of the authors here are young people in middle school, so it is rare to have such achievements. However, what we should pay attention to is that we cannot just call out for ourselves. Since we are in the realm of literature and art, we should have the skills to overcome. Finally, I would like to say to the members of the Duckweed Shadow Society that young people living in this transitional period have many sorrows, but we should not erase our lives just for this. I feel that there is a waste of time for some young people who like to write complaints. I hope that you will not be so sentimental in the whole article, and you must actively express the emotion of upward efforts, which is what we hope for.

Shanghai Market

Business News 214

▲ The New World Hotel declares that Shanghai is full of hotels with similar facilities. Only this hotel can make guests feel truly happy in spirit. The grand and magnificent auditorium is adorned with Xu Zhengbai's landscape paintings and Huang Taixuan's collected couplets, which are particularly elegant and pleasant. It is a well-known venue for exhibitions of paintings and calligraphy by famous Shanghai figures. Whenever celebrations and banquets are held, and guest performances are staged, the hall is always packed but never crowded, which shows the spaciousness of the auditorium.

▲ Jinlili Zhongshi Old Ziyang Temple on Sanma Road declares that this shop has been established for more than 100 years and has been manufacturing famous flower dew wines, seasonal foods, fine official gift pickles, canned sweets, etc. The business is prosperous and famous far and wide. Recently, in order to facilitate customers and expand sales, a branch has been specially set up on East Seward Road (north of Zhonghongqiao). It opened on March 21 and held a month-long sale, making business even more prosperous.

Theater News 215

▲ Arc Star Film Company declares that the company has moved to 505 Jiangwan Road and has greatly expanded its operations. It is working day and night with all its might. Recently, the film "The Legend of Jin Tai," produced by Huang Jiaojun, directed by Lu Yeyuan, and starring Qian Siying and Bao Gusong, will be completed at the end of this month. This play has a lot of chivalrous spirit. The company has spared no effort or financial resources to film "The Legend of Jin Tai" into a feature film, not to make the audience superstitious about gods and monsters, but to make the audience learn from the heroic spirit and chivalrous style in the film.

Calligraphy News 216

▲ Calligraphy is the highest art in China. Since the overthrow of the Qing Dynasty, the academy style has been neglected. Most young people tend to follow unorthodox paths to deceive themselves. Even those who are willing to follow the right path are plagued by a lack of teachers and wander astray. Mr. Wu Yi of Suzhou has deep knowledge of the six methods of calligraphy and is respected by all walks of life. He is also tireless in guiding the younger generation. Recently, at the urging of Mr. Zhang Yipeng, a calligraphy correspondence course department has been specially established to broaden education. Those who aspire to learn calligraphy should not miss this rare and good teacher. The address for correspondence is Mr. Wu Luping, Jukangzhuang, Tianjin Road, Shanghai. Detailed regulations will be sent upon request.

Notice from the Shanghai Market Editorial Department 217

(1) Merchants, doctors, film companies, theaters, and calligraphers should send their manuscripts to the Shanghai Market Department.

(2) Merchants, film companies, theaters, calligraphers, and doctors should affix their seals to the manuscripts as proof, otherwise they will not be published.

(3) Long film reviews will be slightly compensated as usual, calculated at one yuan per thousand words.
